{}Social Studio & Radian6{}
{}KEY TAKEAWAY:{}
Social Studio and Radian6 are built on the same platform = {}Your login details work for both!{}
URL:
<lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId4&quot;/&gt;">Socialstudio.radian6.com</lnk-c>
Use for:
Publishing content – Add icons
Engaging with posts from social accounts
Social listening/ Analyzing results
URL: <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId5&quot;/&gt;">login.radian6.com</lnk-c>
Use for:
Deep dive analysis for social listening
{}Explain the connection between Salesforce Marketing Cloud, Social Studio and Radian6{}
{}Speaker1:{}
<size val="1200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}Understanding the connection between Social Studio and Radian6 is also important.{}
</font></size>Social Studio and Radian6 are two separate interfaces but are built on the same platform.
<size val="1200"> <font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{} {}This means that if you create a topic profile within the Radian6 application, it will be available in Social Studio and vice versa.
As well, all users you add in Social Studio will also be available in Radian6.
The difference is that the Social Studio interface is the one-stop shop for all things Marketing Cloud Social.
It is here where you can create and collaborate on content with your team and then publish it to your social accounts.
You can also engage with posts on your social accounts, and listen and analyze conversations that are happening around your brand.
For most users, this is all you will need. </font></size>
If, however, you need to conduct a deep dive analysis on your topic profiles you may want to use the Radian6 analysis dashboard.
It is currently slightly more customizable than Social Studio.
For the purpose of this webinar series we are going to focus on Social Studio.
9
{}Social Studio:{}
{}Log In{}
{}Explain the connection between Salesforce Marketing Cloud, Social Studio and Radian6{}
{}Speaker1:{}
{}There are two ways to log into Social Studio and the way you choose will depend on which Marketing Cloud products you have access to.{}
{}If you have just purchased MC social Studio, you will log in via socialstudio.radian6.com.{}
{}If you have access to the Marketing Cloud (which includes email, journey builder, etc), you can log in through that application as well.{}
10
{}Workspaces{}
Before you can really get the most out of  Social Studio you need to understand two basic concepts, workspaces and User Roles.
11
{}Social Studio:{}
{}Workspaces{}
{}KEY TAKEAWAY:{}
Social Studio and Radian6 are built on same platform = {}Your login details work for both!{}
Workspaces:
Key to organizing your teams and{} the social accounts they work on.
- Only {}Full Users {}and {}Super Users {}can create workspaces
<size val="1200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}Workspaces are the key to organizing your teams and the social accounts they work on.{}
{}They are the </font></size><size val="2200"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}core component of Social Studio.
In a workspace, you will be able to:</font></eff-l></size>
1) View a calendar of posts from that workspace’s social accounts
2) Compose, schedule, and publish content for that workspace’s social accounts
3) Compose drafts for later use
4) View performance for the workspace’s social accounts
5) Add notes to communicate with other members who have access to the workspace
6) Use approval rules to preview and approve content before it goes live
7) Engage with posts made to that workspace’s social accounts or brought in by a social media search
<size val="1200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Workspaces are associated with specific social accounts.
For example, if your company offers a rewards program, and has a twitter account and facebook page associated with that program, you could create a Rewards workspace and only bring in those accounts.
</font></size>You might also have Twitter and Facebook customer support social accounts<size val="1200"> .<font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">You could then create a workspace just to handle customer support issues and ensure the right users have access.
There are countless ways to organize your workspaces, you just need to think about what works best for your company.</font></size>
12
{}Adding A Social Channel{}
{}Once you have determined the Workspaces you will need, you will need to add social channels to those workspaces.{}
{}Adding Social Channels to your Social Studio account is easy!{}
In the Workspace page, you will click on the Gear icon where you want the new social channel added.
Once you have navigated to the + Add New option – which I will show in the upcoming demo – you will complete the necessary steps to add your channel.
Channels available to add to your Social Studio account are Facebook, Twitter, LinkedIn, Google+,  YouTube, and Instagram.
The screen shots above show the screens you would see if you were adding Facebook to your account.
13
{}User Roles{}
After you determine what workspaces you will need, you need to think about who will have access to those workspaces, and what their roles should be.
14
{}Social Studio:{}
{}Organization User Roles{}
{}Social studio uses a User Role based permission set.{}
There are three types of user roles that impact what users can access, add, or update in the organization:
This graph depicts the level of access each user role has.
The three levels are 1) Super Users, 2) Full Users and 3) Basic Users.
<size val="2200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">A Super User has full create, view, edit and disable/delete permissions on all areas of the Social Studio organization.</font></size>
<size val="1200"> As you can see, they can also:</size>
<size val="1200"> 1) </size><size val="2200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Manage users and user settings, assign users to workspaces, and force password resets</font></size>
2) Edit and view all workspaces
3) Edit and delete all macros
4) Edit all user records
<size val="2200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;"> 5) Add social accounts</font></size><size val="1200"> </size>
<size val="2200">A Full User is the default user level for new users.
Full Users can create most types of resources, and can edit and delete the content they own</size><size val="1200">.
They can create and edit their own macros, and view the content of of workspaces they are members of.</size>
A Basic User can view other users in the organization, but can only change their own personal information.
Basic users also have the following abilities:
1) View content in workspaces they are a member of
2) View and edit any posts they have created
<size val="2200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Basic Users cannot change any of the organization’s settings.</font></size><size val="1200"> </size>
If you are the primary user or admin of your Social Studio account, you will want to be set up as a Super User..
As you can see, Super users have full reign, while basic users have limited access.
If you are a super user it’ll be your job to set up the workspaces and assign users to those workspaces.
15
{}Social Studio:{}
{}Workspace Permissions{}
Users can be added to workspaces.
Permissions in workspaces are separate from the organization user role.
You can set the amount of access each user has within a workspace by using Workspace permissions.
The levels are:
{}Admin{}:
An Admin of a workspace can manage users, social accounts, permissions, settings, labels and publish content in all accounts in the workspace.
{}Contributor{}:
This member can publish and engage with social accounts in the workspace.
They cannot manage workspace settings, add users, or add social accounts, but they can modify user settings.
{}Limited member{}:
This member can view content in the workspace (including the calendar and performance) but cannot publish to the social accounts.
However, you can edit their user permissions to enable them to engage or publish from some or all of the social accounts in the workspace.
{}{}It’s important to remember that:{}{}
{}{}The same social account can be added to more than one workspace{}{}
{}{}Users can be members of  more than one workspace{}{}
{}{}Workspace members can have different permissions in different workspaces{}{}
To set workspace roles simply click on the workspace name, click the cog setting, and then select Users.
From here you can add users to the workspace, set their workspace role and delete users from the workspace.
16
{}Social Studio:{}
{}User Avatars{}
Personalize your representation in Social Studio
Help colleagues put a face to a name with User Avatars.
You can:
Easily upload and switch out images, or keep the default
See your chosen image as a permanent menu fixture
Help colleagues quickly recognize one another within the user list
Notes
Does not support animated gifs or advanced image editing
Super users cannot upload images on behalf of other users
Once users are added they can now create their own avatars.
Avatars can be uploaded to in My Settings.
This feature allows colleagues to easily identify each other within the user list.

{}Speaker1:{}
{}So now that we’ve talked through the basic set up of Social Studio and how to access it, let’s log into the app.{}
{}{}Welcome Screen:{}{}
{}Once you log in the first screen you’ll see is the wizard to help you create a workspace.{}
This screen may vary depending on your user role.
For example, Super users will be able to create  a new workspace, For a basic user, this button would be greyed out.
You’ll also notice two buttons along the top.
One is for workspaces, which we’re currently in, the other is Performance.
This is where you come to run cross-workspace reports.
{}Up in the right hand corner you will notice your name{}.
{}This is where you come to check personal and organizational settings.{}
Here, you will also be able to see what tenant you are logged into and your User Role.
If you click on My Settings you can change your password, or change your email address.
You can also change your language preference.
To check organizational settings, reclick your name.
Then click the Admin cog.
In here, again depending on your user role, you will have access to add new social accounts, create macros, add and manage users and manage the organizational settings such as your time zone.
{}Let’s add a new user.{}
Staying within the Admin settings you will see a section called users.
We’re going to click on “Add new”.
Fill in the new users display name, which will be the name that shows up within the application, User name, which is what they will need to log in, and their email.
The language and time zone will autopopulate based on the organizational settings you have already configured.
However, if these settings do not work for the user, simply choose the correct values from the drop down menus.
You will then select  their role from either Super User, Full User or Basic.
Set the user as Active so they now have access to Social Studio.
Or if you need to deactivate a user, you would select Deactivate.
The final step is selecting which workspaces the user will have access to.
Simply click “Add to Workspace”  and select from the list of available workspaces.
{}Next let’s add a social account{}.
Note, in order to add a social account you must be the page admin of that account.
You will need to authorize Social Studio to have access to the account.
{}Now we’re ready to create a workspace{}.
So lets return to the workspace screen by clicking the Social Studio logo.
We’re going to click “Create New”.
Now we’re going to name our workspace.
Remember to name it something that reflects the product or function you will be working on.
Let’s name ours _____.
You can also upload a picture and provide a description of the workspace.
Once you’ve chosen a name click “Next”.
You will now be prompted to add the social accounts you want in this workspace.
Simply search for the name and click on it.
The social account will appear on the right.
Once all accounts are added click Next.
You will then be prompted to add workspace members.
These will be the individuals who will need to have access to this particular workspace.
You can change the user’s permissions and access once added.
To delete a user, simply click the X next to their name.
Once you’ve added all the users you will be taken to a summary screen.
Here you can check to ensure everything is set up they way you want it.
If everything looks good, click Finish.
And now you have your first workspace.
Once you click finish you will be directed to the publish calendar (if you have publish) or the Engage tab if you do not have Publish.
In this view you can see the name of the workspace in the top left.
You can return to the welcome screen by clicking ______.
You can also navigate between Publish, Engage and Analyze by clicking on the names along the top.
To access Workspace Settings, simply click the Cog next to the workspace name.
Within this area you can manage any settings that pertain to that particular workspace.
From this view you can also set up approval rules and labels for outgoing content.
You may want to use approval rules if you require content to be reviewed and approved prior to posting.
As well, you may want to label your content a specific way for easier tracking.

{}You can now create a topic profile within Analyze.{}
A topic profile is a collection of keywords or phrases that you define.
These keywords can be grouped into categories such as Brand, competitors and Industry or they may be left uncategorized.
<size val="1200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Due to the connection between the two systems, Topic profiles that you build within analyze can be opened within the Radian6 app and vice versa.

</font></size>If you use these features in Radian6, the data will show in Analyze, but you will not have access there to modify the data.

{}Explain the connection between Salesforce Marketing Cloud, Social Studio and Radian6{}
{}Speaker1:{}
There are six types of dashboards you can create:
1) Twitter Account Summary  2) Social Listening Summary, 3) Facebook Account Summary  4) LinkedIn Account Summary 5) Google+ Account Summary and 6) YouTube Account Summary.
Each summary dashboard provides overviews of volume, sentiment trends and emerging keywords.
Some differences do occur between the dashboards based on where the information is coming from.
For example, the emerging key words from  the twitter account summary dashboard are pulled from up to 50 twitter accounts, where the emerging keywords from a Social Listening summary account dashboard are from a social listening topic profile.
Key Note:
Up to 10 Google+ accounts can be used to create a dashboard

{}Start with the basics:{}
{}Dashboard Cards – <size val="2400">Engagement Summary </size>{}
Twitter Account Summary
Social Listening Summary
{}Explain the connection between Salesforce Marketing Cloud, Social Studio and Radian6{}
{}Speaker1:{}
The Engagement Summary card shows the overall engagement (volume) and breakdown of post volume by interactions or media type.
The data displayed varies depending on the type of dashboard.
For example:
For a Twitter Account Summary, the card will display:
Overall volume of your twitter account(s)
Post count
And the percentages and daily averages for tweets, mentions(including retweets, @mentions, and replies) and direct messages sent and received.
For  a Social Listening Summary, the card will display:
Overall volume of your topic profile  and post count
And the percentages and daily averages for various media types including twitter, facebook, blogs, mainstream news, forum, forum replies, aggregator, buy/sell
Note:
There will be subtle differences for each of the four dashboard types, this is just an example of two.

{}Speaker1:{}
{}Alright, so now that we know the basic set up of Analyze, let’s log into the app to see it in action.{}
{}{}Welcome Screen:{}{}
{}When you log in the first screen you will see is the workspace calendar view.{}
{}Check to ensure you are in the correct workspace.{}
{}Navigate to Analyze.{}
{}As we mentioned, you will be taken to a clear screen and prompted to create a dashboard.{}
So here is where you choose what type of dashboard you would like to create either a Twitter Summary dashboard or a Social Listening Summary dashboard.
Let’s begin by creating a dashboard based on our Twitter social account.
When you click on Twitter Account Summary you will see all the twitter social accounts available within the workspace.
Choose the one you want to analyze.
A dashboard will populate with an analysis of all the data from the social account you chose.
You will see the 6 cards we discussed previously that are autopopulated with the results.
You can easily drill down and filter the data from here.
For example, to filter the data in the “posts over time” card you can simply check which boxes you want to see and uncheck those you don’t want to see.
The same goes for sentiment and sentiment over time.
Simply check or uncheck the data to get the view you want to see.
For posts shown in the feed, you can use Post Inspector to view any workflow or labels that have been applied to the post.
And drill down further.
You can now also add workflow to the posts from this view.
You can also use analyze to bring in data from a topic profile you have created.
As I mentioned earlier, topic profiles can be created either within social studio or within the Radian6 app.
Topic profiles created in Radian6 are available within Social Studio and vice versa.
Because this webinar series focuses on Social Studio, I’ll demonstrate how to create a topic profile from within analyze.
Click on the Admin setting cog.
From there we add a new topic profile.
It’ll prompt us to identify our key words.
We can set proximity to those key words.
We can also filter by language, media type or region.
Simply click, create new topic profile and its done.
Now that you have created your Topic Profile and added it to your workspace, you can create a Social Listening Dashboard.
Let’s go back to Analyze, and click create New Dashboard.
This time we are going to select Social Listening Dashboard.
Note the EMV on the topic profile (since you may have a limit based on your entitlement).
Choose the topic profile you want and the dashboard will populate.
You’ll notice the card names are all the same, but the data coming in is slightly different.
For example, the data in the Post Volume card will show the % of posts from Facebook, Twitter, and other media sources instead of “tweets”, DMs etc.
I{}f you create more than one dashboard you can simply go back and forth by using the dropdown menu at the top of the screen.{}
This is similar to the workspace menu  where you can choose from recent dashboards you have created or select the Dashboard Gallery, which is like the welcome screen for workspaces, but will show you all dashboards.
To delete a dashboard simply click on the Cog on the upper right while you are viewing the dashboard.
From the drop down menu choose, Delete dashboard.

{}Speaker1:{}
Welcome to the Getting Started with Marketing Cloud Social webinar series.
The objective of this third webinar is to introduce you to the publish component of Social Studio.
<size val="2400"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Today we will cover how to filter and adjust the calendar view, how to create, schedule, and post content, how to view post details on the calendar, and how to use the note function for effective team management.</font></size><size val="1600"> </size>
{}Let’s Get Started{}
8
<size val="3200">{}Publish:{}
{}Social Content Marketing</size><br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr sz=&quot;3200&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" /><size val="2700"><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;009DDC&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Plan, Source, Execute, and Measure Differentiated Social Campaigns</fill-sd></size>{}
<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;009DDC&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Collaborative Team Planning:
</fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;7C868D&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Coordinate via a unified calendar to align and execute social campaigns.</fill-sd>
<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;009DDC&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Protect and Safeguard the Brand:
</fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;7C868D&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Customize approval rules to review social content. </fill-sd>
<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;009DDC&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Find Compelling Content:
</fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;7C868D&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Access stock images, trending web stories, and customer-specific sources of content via our open platform and an ecosystem of partner apps.</fill-sd>
What do we mean by Publish?
Publish is the name of our Social Content Marketing product.
You can use Publish for collaborative team planning on a unified calendar, protect your company’s brand by customizing approval rules for social content, and find relevant, trendy and compelling content by accessing sources via our open platform and ecosystem of partner apps.
Let’s first review the basic layout of Publish and its key features  and then I’ll demonstrate how to set it up.
{}Start with the basics:{}
{}Publish{}
{}Social Studio Publish is one of the three key functionalities of Social Studio.{}
{}The other two being Listen and Analyze, and Engage.{}
{}It’s important to note that not everyone has access to Publish as it is purchased separately from those other two.{}
{}The primary purpose of Publish is to help companies coordinate the launch of their social media content across teams and social accounts.{}
{}When you log into Social Studio you will be taken to the publish calendar view of the last workspace you were in.{}
{}This view will show you (1) a view of all pending content launches across multiple social accounts within the workspace.{}
{}Date ranges and calendar view settings are found on the top right corner (2/3).{}
{}Calendar filters including social accounts and approval status can be found on the left.{}
{}On the far left you’ll also find the icons to create content, check performance of a social account, review drafts and view content that has recently been shared.{}
10
{}Creating Content{}
{}Facebook Gating:{}
Useful for companies with one Global Facebook page.
{}Feed Targeting:{}
Helps with targeting and improves engagement
{}LinkedIn Targeting:{}
Target your audience by industry, function, seniority, {}and/or geography
{}Twitter:{}
Target your whole audience to maximize {}awareness
{}YouTube and Google +:{}
Track performance including views, {}comments, link clicks, likes and dislikes
{}Instagram:{}
Track likes and comments for the {}visualization of your brand
Within Publish there are currently five types of posts you can create:
Facebook, Twitter and LinkedIn, Youtube, Google+, and Instagram. In.
Each type of post provides a different ability to  target and engage your intended audience.
It is important to note, that to publish to Instagram you must your our Social Studio mobile app because Instagram doesn’t provide API access to allow partners, like ourselves, to publish to their network.
<font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">For example:
Facebook provides two targeting options:
Facebook gating or Feed targeting.
Gating is a great option if you have one global Facebook page for your company.
</font>Gating a post makes it viewable to users within specific countries or who speak specific languages.
Once published, a gated post will only appear in the newsfeed and on the page to users within the chosen demographic.
<font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Feed targeting is a little different.
This is a great option to use if you want the content to live on your facebook page and viewable to all users, but you only want to send the content to a specific demographic.
By t</font>argeting posts to match various marketing segments you can greatly improve a post’s engagement.
LinkedIn Targeting lets you target a LinkedIn Post's audience by company size, industry, function, seniority and/or geography.
This is a great feature to use if you are recruiting talent for your company and only want to target users within a particular function, such as marketing.
With Twitter posts the content is available and shareable by all.
It is a great way to maximize the exposure of your content.
11
{}Repost and Cross-Post Efficiently{}
<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;009DDC&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Duplicate Posts:
</fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;7C868D&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">It’s important to publish great content regularly and the easiest way to do that is to use the “Duplicate” option to post to the same network or cross-post and optimize it for another network. </fill-sd>
Duplicating posts is a great time saver in your busy day.
You can re-use textual posts across networks, and in the case of video posts, you can upload the video once and share it to another network without uploading it again.
I will show how you do this in our demo.
If you duplicate a Facebook post, all of the metadata like gating, targeting, and labeling is maintained and used for the subsequent post.
If you are duplicating a YouTube post for Facebook, you can add gating and targeting criteria to optimize your Facebook post.
{}Collaboration{}
The product also provides an excellent solution for teams to collaborate on posts.
{}Calendar{}
The Publish calendar is the obvious tool to use for collaboration amongst teams.
The calendar allows you to see when content is scheduled to go live for each social account that is added to that particular workspace.
You can filter the calendar a variety of ways including, by date, post status, and social accounts.
Quick tip to share:
Typically we recommend to segment your social accounts and teams into different workspaces to help keep things  organized, however, there is a use case for creating a workspace that houses all your social accounts.
Some companies do this so that they can see the schedule for all content across all workspaces.
Typically, content is not created in this workspace, but it does allow an all encompassing calendar view of all scheduled and draft form content.
Some other key collaboration features I’d suggest you take advantage of are the notes feature and shared content.
{}Notes{}
<font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">The notes feature allows any team member to provide a quick update on the post.
You can access notes by clicking on any calendar date. (click 1) The note is housed in the post inspector window that pops up (click 2, 3).
Leave </font><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">n</font>otes for team members in your Workspace to view, edit, or remove Posts.
Notes can be up to 256 characters in length and be used to document anything such as:
-Notes to other team members
-Questions
-Comments
-Suggestions
You can also see who the note is from and respond directly in the post inspector.
13
{}Collaboration{}
Shared Content
{}Shared Content{}
<font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Shared content is the ultimate tool for collaboration and promoting team success.
</font>Shared Content are posts and content that are saved in a special folder within Social Studio so they can be reused and shared among other members in a workspace.
Using Shared Content is important in that it allows users to reuse and modify previous created top performing content without having to recreate it from scratch every time, possibly introducing errors or inconsistencies in style, info and voice.
If a post needs to be reused, shared content can be created from a published, unpublished, scheduled or unscheduled posts.
14
{}Performance and Tracking{}
The final key feature I want to highlight is the ability to track the performance of your content.
Once your content is posted, the post's performance can be measured and tracked to analyze the effectiveness and if the post is accomplishing the targets or milestones you may have established.
Content Performance can be measured and tracked in different locations within Social Studio:
1) Individual post level
2) Workspace content performance, which reports on content performance for a workspace
3) Cross workspace performance, which reports on content performance for all the workspaces in the organization
If you want to see how well your posted content is performing at an individual level,  you can simply click on the post and the stats will be available in the post inspector window.
Here you can view overall totals and breakdown of reach, clicks, engagements and engagement rate.
As well you can see the breakdown of negative feedback.
15
{}Performance and Tracking- <br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr&gt;&lt;a:latin typeface=&quot;Arial&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;34&quot; charset=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:ea typeface=&quot;ＭＳ Ｐゴシック&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;-97&quot; charset=&quot;-128&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:cs typeface=&quot;Arial&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;34&quot; charset=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:rPr&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" /><size val="2000">Workspace Content Performance</size>{}
{}Summary{}:
A <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId6&quot;/&gt;">summary</lnk-c> of how the social accounts attached to the workspace are doing over the past seven days and cannot be customized
{}Post Reports:{}
<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx1&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">- Can be </fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;000000&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">for all posts, Facebook posts only, Twitter posts only or LinkedIn posts only</fill-sd>
- Can be customized, sorted and exported
To access workspace content performance tracking, click the performance icon within the desired workspace. (click 1)
There are two key reporting areas within this section:
A <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId3&quot;/&gt;">summary</lnk-c> of how the social accounts attached to the workspace are doing over the past seven days and cannot be customized
<size val="1200"><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx1&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;"><lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId4&quot;/&gt;">2) Post Reports</lnk-c> – which can be </fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;000000&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">for all posts, Facebook posts only, Twitter posts only or LinkedIn posts only and can be <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId5&quot;/&gt;">customized</lnk-c>, <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId5&quot;/&gt;">sorted</lnk-c></size><size val="2200"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;"> and </font></eff-l></size><size val="1200"><lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId5&quot;/&gt;">exported</lnk-c></size><size val="2200"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">.</font></eff-l></size></fill-sd>
16
{}Performance and Tracking- <br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr&gt;&lt;a:latin typeface=&quot;Arial&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;34&quot; charset=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:ea typeface=&quot;ＭＳ Ｐゴシック&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;-97&quot; charset=&quot;-128&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:cs typeface=&quot;Arial&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;34&quot; charset=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:rPr&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" /><size val="2000">Cross Workspace Performance</size>{}
{}Post Report{}:

{}Account Reports:{}
<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx1&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">-</fill-sd>Presents page level metrics for selected Facebook accounts, Facebook user demographics and Twitter account metrics
Visit <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId6&quot;/&gt;">Social Studio User Guide </lnk-c>for more info
To access Cross workspace content performance tracking, click the performance icon on the workspace Welcome page. (click 1)
Cross Workspace performance reports are designed to show the performance of social accounts in a Social Studio tenant.
The reports, which can be downloaded and customized, are categorized into:
<lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId3&quot;/&gt;">{}1) Cross Workspace Post Reports</lnk-c>{} - Presents metrics for Facebook Post Impressions and Engagement and Twitter Engagement over a specified time range
<lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId4&quot;/&gt;">{}2) Account Reports</lnk-c>{} - Presents page level metrics for selected Facebook accounts, Facebook user demographics and Twitter account metrics
For more detailed information on these types of reports check out the user guide on the H&T portal

{}Now let’s move into the app to show you how Publish works!{}
{}The picture here shows the end state of some published content.{}
{}Let’s go into the app and demo out the steps.{}
{}{}Welcome Screen:{}{}
{}When you log in the first screen you will see is the workspace calendar view.{}
This will be the calendar of the last workspace you were in.
Make sure to check that you are in the correct workspace.
You can check what workspace your in by looking at the name beside the Social Studio logo.
To switch to another workspace, simply click on the arrow beside the current workspace name.
The drop down menu will show you a list of your recent workspaces, and also give you the option to return to the main workspace menu.
In this drop down menu you can also access workspace settings by clicking on the Cog.
{}So let’s go back to the calendar view and I’ll show you how to adjust the date settings.{}
The calendar can easily be changed to  show a view for a day, week or month. (demonstrate).
{}You can further filter the content you’re viewing by clicking the “Filter” button.{}
This will allow you to filter by Social Account, content status or content labels, authors or  media type.
For example, if I just wanted to see content being posted to my facebook social account, I would only select that social account.
If I only wanted to see content being created by me, I would go down to the area titles “Match any of these authors” and select only myself.
You could also filter it to only view content that is published or only see content that is currently scheduled. (demonstrate).
{}You can also add notes within the calendar.{}
Simply click on the date you want to add a note to and you will see the option show up.
{}So now let’s learn how to actually create a post within Publish.{}
Along the left hand side you’ll notice the 6 “action” buttons we reviewed previously.
To create content, we’re going to click on the bright green one.
Lets create a post in Twitter.
From here  we’re able to select which account the content will be posted to, we can create our content and upload a picture if we want.
We can click the button “get content from apps” if we want to upload a stock photo or use Trendspottr to see what is currently trending online.
Note, you will need to have an account with these apps in order to use them..
We can choose whether we want to publish this post immediately or choose a later date.
Also, we have the option of shortening the link if we want.
And, we can apply a label which can be useful for filtering and reporting.
Once all the fields are filled out you can either save the post as a draft, or you can publish.
When you go back to the calendar view you will see your post on the date you selected.
Let’s try another example but this time let’s create content for LinkedIn.
We’ll follow the same steps except this time we’re going to add a target.
This means we can select who we want to view the content.
The target group can be based on geolocation, job function, industry, company size and seniority.
So for our example let’s target people on linkedin from the Greater Boston Area.
We’re going to publish and now when we go to the calendar view, we can see our post is ready to go.
And my boss and the other co-workers who have access to this workspace can see what’s planned to be released this month.
{}Now, once a post is created, you may need to edit it.{}
For example, maybe the sale you were going to promote has moved to another date or been cancelled all together.
To edit a post, simply click on the post you want to edit in the calendar view.
The post inspector window will appear.
About half way down you will see “Edit”.
Click on it.
This will take you to the “create content view”.
Simply edit the changes you want to make and click save.
To view any draft posts click on the draft icon on the left, then select the post you want to edit.
This will bring you to the “Create content” screen and you can alter the post and schedule it from here.
Alright, so now that we’ve created a post and published it, we’ll want to keep track of it’s performance.
This can be done one of two ways.
If you just want a quick view of stats for an individual post you can simply click on the post in the calendar.
This will cause a window to appear on the right.
Scroll down and you’ll see a performance summary for that post.
If you want to pull a report on all posts, click the performance icon on the left.
This will provide you with an overall view of performance by social account.
If you want to export the data you can click a Post Report.
This can show all posts, or posts separated by the available social accounts.
We’re going to export the performance of all posts.
So, I will click on “All Posts”, which takes me to a table view showing the stats for each post that has been made on the workspace.
By clicking “Filters” we can choose the date range we want to see.
So I’ll select all posts from the last 2 weeks.
I’ll then click export to a .csv file.
Then I’ll have the data to analyze in excel.
{}The next area we’ll quickly review is Tasks.{}
If you have actions related to approval rules, they will be displayed here.
Now, you may not have approval rules set up in your tenant, and that’s ok.
However, if you do, when they are triggered, the posts will show up here while they wait for approval.
Approval rules can be found in the workspace settings. (demonstrate how to get there).
So, if you are the approver, you can go to tasks to see which posts you need to approve.
Let’s reject this one. (demonstrate).
<size val="1200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}The final left hand option is Shared Content.{}
Sharing content that has performed successfully, such as a post that gets a lot of engagement, amongst </font></size><size val="2200"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">other teams can be quite valuable.
By sharing the content with other workspace, those teams can then simply edit as they require and hope to get similar results.
When you click on the shared content icon, you will be able to view all shared content and which workspaces it has been shared with (demonstrate).
You can also see the content stats such as how many times it has been used, total engagements, average engagements and the overall engagement rates.
So let’s decide to use this content.
We are then taken to the edit content screen and we can change or schedule as we wish.</font></eff-l></size>

{}Objectives:{}
<br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr sz=&quot;2800&quot;&gt;&lt;a:latin typeface=&quot;Arial&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;34&quot; charset=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:cs typeface=&quot;Arial&quot; pitchFamily=&quot;34&quot; charset=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:rPr&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />{}Getting Started:{}

Understand and create macros
Import topic profiles created in Analyze
{}Objective Slide{}
{}Speaker1:{}
During this webinar we are going to touch on a variety of topics including how to create columns and tabs specific to your business needs.
We will introduce you to Post Inspector, teach you how to create macros, and how to access your topic profiles from Analyze so you can respond to posts about your brand appropriately,
{}Let’s Get Started{}
8
{}Start with the basics:{}
{}Engage{}
{}Navigating Engage{}
{}Speaker1:{}
{}Engage is one of the three functions available in Marketing Cloud Social Studio.{}
{}It is here where you will be able respond to posts about your brand or apply workflow to ensure they are dealt with or at least labeled appropriately.{}
{}Let’s review Engage’s interface.{}
{}To get to the Engage interface simply click on the workspace you want to be in.{}
{}You will automatically be brought to the calendar view of the workspace.{}
{}From there simply click Engage (1) from them top banner.{}
{}If it is your first time using Engage in the workspace you will be prompted to add a column.{}
{}Columns (2) can be comprised of any of your social accounts or even topic profiles you have created in Analyze.{}
{}As a reminder, Topic Profiles are social media searches of content that might not show up in your standard social accounts.{}
{}To add a column simply click (3) the “Add Column” icon.{}
{}This is prompt you to select a topic profile or social account you have already created.{}
{}Within each column you will see each post (4) being brought in about that specific topic.{}
{}If you click on a post, the Post Inspector screen will appear (5).{}
{}Post inspector allows you to apply an action or workflow to the post.{}
{}Here you can take actions such as responding, reposting, or direct messaging the sender.{}
{}You can also  label the post to make for easier reporting, apply sentiment and use workflow to ensure the right person responds.{}
{}You can also apply a macro to the post from the Post Inspector panel.{}
{}We will discuss Macros in more detail once we move into the app.{}
{}Along the bottom of the screen you will see “My tab” (6).{}
{}Tabs are used to organize your columns in to specific categories.{}
{}For example, one tab may contain columns from your Facebook social accounts and another tab may have columns with conversations from your Twitter social accounts.{}
{}You can simply add a tab by clicking the “+” icon.{}
{}Once clicked, you can name the tab whatever you’d like.{}
9
{}Understanding Columns{}
{}Navigating Engage{}
{}Speaker1:{}
Let’s take a minute to understand the different types of columns you can have, where the information comes from, and how they are beneficial.
With Engage you can pull in activity from your Facebook, Twitter and LinkedIn social accounts {}(click 1{}).
Remember, in order to have access to these accounts they need to be added first to your organization settings and then added to the appropriate workspace.
You can add social accounts to a workspace within the workspace settings. ({}click 2){}.
By pulling in data from your social accounts you are able to engage and respond to posts and comments directed at your company.
Topic profiles can also be pulled into an Engage Column.
Quick reminder, Topic profiles are customized searches based on a set of keywords that you define.
The key difference between Topic Profile columns and Social account columns is that the information being pulled into the Topic Profiles are based on the defined keywords and the comments that are pulled in may not be directed specifically at your company.
This allows you to comment and engage with posts that would not normally be pulled into your social accounts.
As well, you an have a mixture of social media types pulled into a topic profile.
There are many use cases for using topic profiles but some examples include:
1) identifying potential leads, 2) recruiting talent and 3) proactive customer service.
If you remember from the Listen and Analyze webinar, there are two places where you can create topic profiles 1) organizational settings and workspace settings {}(click 3)){}.
Topic Profiles created in Organizational settings will need to be imported into the desired workspace before they are available to use in that workspace.
You can import a topic profile within the workspace settings cog.
10
{}Collaboration, Workflow, and Macros{}
{}Workflow and Macros:{}
Engaging with a post is essentially performing an action to the post by replying, retweeting, deleting, etc.
Workflow management refers to the prescribed actions you assign to social media posts.
For example: assigning posts with a specific hashtag to a specific person in your organization.
The post can be engaged from either the Engage column or from within the Post Inspector. (click 1) Here you choose to reply, retweet, DM (Click 2) change the status of the post.
(Click 3) Set the post priority (Click 4) and Assign it to the appropriate resource. (click 5).
A new feature recently added is real-time collaboration.
This feature provides real-time updates to show when co-workers inspect posts for engagement allowing teams to know who is online and what posts they’re working on {}(click 6){}.
Part of this feature includes automated column updates where columns detect and automatically remove posts that no longer match your filter settings.
Macros enable more efficient workflow by using one Macro button to apply a variety of custom actions to multiple posts at the same time.(Click 6) Macros save time and provides a more uniform approach to how a team engages with posts.
(For Twitter and Facebook).
Engagement Macros can be created by either a Super User or by a Full User from the Organization Admin section (with the <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId3&quot;/&gt;">proper Permission levels</lnk-c>).
Full Users can only create and edit their own macros and Super Users can create and edit any macro.
Engage Macros can be used to automate and streamline various actions such as:
Assigning multiple post entries with a certain hashtag to a certain person AND changing the status to "Reviewed, determining best response" AND setting the priority to High AND assigning a specific post label AND changing the classification to "Customer Lead”.
Note:
Publishing macros and Engage macros are different and cannot be used interchangablely.

<size val="1200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}Navigate to Engage by clicking on the Engage tab up top (</font></size><size val="2200"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}Show initial blank starting view).

The view is private to you and you can create unlimited tabs and columns.
Important note:
Check the workspace you are in.
You’ll automatically be returned to the workspace you were last in To navigate to other workspaces simply click on the Workspace name in the top left hand corner next to the Social Studio logo.
The name displayed is the workspace you are currently in.
Once clicked, you can see a list of recent workspaces you have worked on.
You can also click on “All workspaces” to be taken back to the workspace view.
As well, you can create a new workspace directly from here.</font></eff-l></size>
{}Next we’re going to create a Tab:{}
As I mentioned earlier tabs are a great way to organize your social accounts.
For the purpose of this webinar we are going to create a tab for Facebook and a tab for Twitter.
To rename a tab, just click on the arrow beside the tab and you’ll be prompted to either rename or delete the tab.
To add a new tab Simply click on the (+) sign.
You can name your new tab, then click “Add Tab”.
Tabs can be dragged and dropped to customize your desktop and prioritize the most important discussions.
{}Once you have your tab created you’re going to need to create columns.{}
Click the Add column icon.
This will prompt you to choose either a social account or a topic profile you have created.
Because I’m in my facebook tab,  I’m going to add a Facebook social account.
So you can see all the posts on my social account are now displayed in the column.
But what if I want to segment the posts from those that I’ve posted versus those that my customers/ followers have posted.
This may be important to know if I want to take action on any negative posts coming in about my brand or to reply to  customer service issues.
You can segment the data by using filters
{}To apply a filter to a column click the settings cog on the top right of the column.{}
This will cause a screen to pop up on the right.
From here you can add filters, edit social accounts, rename the column or fully delete the column.
Since we want to add a filter, I am going to click on “Filter”.
From here you can filter the column by media type directly related to facebook, such as your posts, comments, inbox messages, replies to comments.
You can also filter by workflow functions such as status, priority, assignment or classification.
I’ll show how to label your posts in a moment.
First, I want a column that shows all the posts my company has created and a column of all the comments we have received.(Demo it).
Let’s do the same thing now, but for a twitter account.
First we’ll create our twitter column.
Then we’ll choose our Twitter social account to bring all the posts.
Let’s filter this column by mentions so we can see who is talking about us, and reach out if we need to.
So we click on the settings cog, then on filter and we only click mentions.
Now we can see who is talking about us.
- Updated April Release:
New sort options:
Oldest first and Filter by Date range.
Customer timeframes limited to 30 days.
{}So, you saw in the filtering options, that you can filter by status, priority etc.{}
{}I now want to show you how to apply those labels to a post.{}
{}This is done in the Post Inspector.{}
To access the Post Inspector, click on any individual post in your column.
The Post Inspector box will show up on the right side of your screen.
From here you can engage with the post by replying, DM, quoting, retweeting or favouriting the post.
Note, these functions are also available directly on the post without going into Post Inspector.
However, you can also apply workflow or a label to a post within the Inspector.
For example, say a post comes in that is negative and you want to ensure it doesn’t get missed.
You could set the status as “Reviewed, determining best response”.
You could then set the priority and assign the post to the appropriate person so they can reach out.
You may also want to apply sentiment, classification or a label which will help with reporting.
So, after we set the status and assign sentiment and classification, you can see that the post in our feed now shows the actions we just took.
When you go back to the Inspector, all the changes are listed in the activity section.
For the Activity section you can also add a note, which will show up on the post in the column.
<size val="1200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}This is a good time to talk about Macros.{}
</font></size><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><size val="2200"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">If you need to take the same actions over and over again, such as assigning positive posts to a specific person and giving them a certain classification or status, you can create a macro.
A macro means you can apply several criteria to a post with just one button click.</font></size>
<size val="1200"> Macros can be created in the main Admin settings.
Click New Macro.
You are going to give the macro a name.
We’ll call ours “____”.
You then choose the workspace you want to assign the macro to.
Since we’re using ____ workspace, I’ll choose that.
Then you simply choose the options you want in your macro.
For example, if we want all postive posts to be assigned to the same person, we’d simply input that criteria, click save and the macro is completed.
Navigate back to your workspace and you will be see the macro is now available in the post inspector.</size></eff-l>
{}Sometimes, you may need to Delete a post.{}
{}Before you choose to delete you’ll want to ensure your have specific guidelines on what posts get deleted.{}
To delete a post  simply click the “trash can” icon.
The post will become greyed out and the next time the column is loaded, the post will be gone.
{}We’ve talked about creating columns with your social accounts like Twitter and Facebook, but you can also show create columns from Topic Profiles{}.
Topic profiles, you’ll remember from the Analyze/ Listen webinar, are customized social searches about any particular topic.
With the appropriate permissions you can create Topic Profiles within Social Studio using Analyze or within the separate app Radian6.
If you need more info on how to create a topic profile, you should check out our many resources or attend the next Listen/ Analyze webinar.
To add a topic profile, go to the workplace settings.
Because Radian6 and Social Studio “talk” to eachother all Topic profiles created in Radian6 are available here and vice versa.
Go back to the workspace and click the engage function.
Add a new column and this time we’ll click Topic Profile.
Select the TP you want to bring in to your column.
You’ll notice all features are the same.
You can use Post Inspector, reply to posts, label them etc.
If you want to get more information on the poster, simply click on their photo icon and you’ll see their bio, twitter stats and all their recent posts.
{}Finally, I just want to show you the create content button.{}
If you are using Publish, you’ll know that this is where you can create a post and put it on your social account.
Simply click, fill in the content you want to publish and select to social account you want to publish to.

{}Table of Contents{}
Welcome to Salesforce!
This Getting Started Workbook was designed to help you get off to a great start and fast track your deployment in 4 steps:
{}Step 1:{}
{}Prepare for Success{} – determine who is involved and how to focus your journey
{}Step 2:{}
{}Create the User Experience -{} adapt Salesforce to enable and improve your business processes
{}Step 3:{}
{}Enable the User Experience with Data{} - import clean data and create valuable reports
{}Step 4:{}
{}Deploy and Empower your Users{} - train, support, motivate, and engage your users by driving business outcomes
Use this workbook to capture your goals, track your set-up checklist, and link to relevant Salesforce resources.
Visit the <hlnk id="rId9" history="1"><rpr id="4">{}Getting Started Quickstart</rpr id="4" transform="close"></hlnk>{}, the central hub of resources aimed at getting you up and running on Salesforce including:
<hlnk id="rId10" history="1"><rpr id="5">{}Getting Started Webinar Series</rpr id="5" transform="close"></hlnk>{} – This interactive webinar series shares best practices and proven approaches to help you implement Salesforce.
The four steps outlined in this workbook align to the four webinars in the series.
<hlnk id="rId11" history="1"><rpr id="5">{}Getting Started Videos</rpr id="5" transform="close"></hlnk>{} – The Getting Started series is available as on demand videos and align with the steps outlined in this workbook.
<hlnk id="rId12" history="1"><rpr id="5">{}Getting Started Community</rpr id="5" transform="close"></hlnk>{} – Join this forum specifically created for new customers to ask questions and get answers from Salesforce experts.
If you have a Premier Success Plan, be sure to visit the <hlnk id="rId13" history="1"><rpr id="5">{}Premier Toolkit</rpr id="5" transform="close"></hlnk>{} for additional resources, including the premier training catalog and role based learning paths.
If you have Premier Success & Administration, be sure to review the Admin Services section for guidance on how to submit a request to your premier administrator to assist with common tasks.

{}Determine your key players{}
Use this worksheet to identify the people who will be critical to making Salesforce a success at your company.
Individuals can have multiple responsibilities.
{}Key Responsibilities{}
{}Key Players{}
{}Executive Sponsor{}
Champions the project and sets the business vision for deployment.
{}Business Process Owner{}
Knows the sales process steps and maps them to Salesforce.
{}System Administrator{}
Configures Salesforce and manages it day to day.
{}Data Analyst{}
Understands current data and owns the consolidation and mapping of data.
{}Champion{}
Serves as liaison to users to ensure Salesforce meets day-to-day needs.

{}Identify and prioritize your business objectives{}

{}1.{}
{}Define your vision statement{}
Define a clear purpose for your Salesforce initiative, drive ongoing commitment, and provide a way to measure and prove results.
Questions to ask:
What will your business look like in 3 to 5 years from now?
What future customer needs do you want to satisfy?
{}My Vision Statement (SAMPLE){}
“Build and maintain long-term relationships with valuable customers by creating personalized experiences across all touch points and by anticipating customer needs and providing customized service.”
“Customer loyalty is our highest priority.”
“Provide the highest level of personalized service and give customers the communication channels they want.”

{}Data Preparation{}
How clean is my data?
Are there duplicate names, companies, etc. that I need to merge?
Export field name columns from Salesforce to create your data import template (no need to change column headers if using ACT, Outlook, GoldMine, Palm Desktop)
Include the record owner ID
Populate required fields
Use valid pick list values (example:
Not Started, In Review, Complete)
Include an import batch field (optional)
Add Created By and Created Date fields (optional, requires a opening a case with Salesforce to open up fields)
Include legacy system data ID (optional)
Examine data and correct errors
Delete duplicates
Correct spelling
Enforce standards
Fill-in incomplete fields

{}Deploy and Empower your Users{}

{}Plan your training{}

{}Determine relevant scenarios{}

{}Sales Rep Training Scenario (Sample){}
{}Scenario{}
{}Functionality{}
Runs her weekly sales meetings with the pipeline report
Reviews her teams’ completed and scheduled activities
Meets with sales rep to review pipeline, activities and lead conversion
Reviews status of top 10 opportunities for the current month
Views selected key opportunities to understand pending steps for close
Uses mobile device to check on monthly sales targets, collaborates with sales reps on opportunities
{}Reports & Dashboards:{}
View and drill down on an opportunity, activity and lead reports
{}Sales Process:{}
Sales stages, update opportunities, contact roles and products
{}Lead Process:{}
Lead status, conversion
{}Activity Tracking:{}
Create/update activities
{}Chatter:{}
Post on opportunity and account records
{}Salesforce1:{}
Today, Dashboards, Post, Opportunities, Collaboration
{}Sales Manager Training Scenario (Sample){}
{}Scenario{}
{}Functionality{}
Contacts leads to determine if they are an ideal prospect and convert
Reviews account, opportunity and activity details before speaking with customer
After customer meetings, updates opportunity sales stages and creates an activity for follow up
Views Opportunity Management dashboard to prepare for meeting with manager
Uses mobile device to view open tasks for the day
{}Reports & Dashboards: {}view and drill down on opportunities
{}Lead Process{}: convert leads, update lead status
{}Sales Process{}:

{}Activity Tracking: {}create/ update activities
{}Chatter: {}post on opportunity and account records

After today’s session you will be equipped to install the Salesforce Marketing Cloud Connector, formerly known as the v5 integration.

{}Salesforce Account Setup{}
{}Speaker 2 (if two speakers):{}
Before you can install the Salesforce Marketing Cloud Connector, ensure that you have a Salesforce.com edition that is either Unlimited, Enterprise or Performance.
<size val="2200"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Please note:
Professional Edition is not supported by the Salesforce Marketing Cloud Connector at this time.
The Professional Edition is supported in the v2 integration which can be installed using the v2 Integration user guide **which can be found on the Help & Training portal for the Salesforce Marketing Cloud**.</font></eff-l></size>
You will also need one of the following Marketing Cloud accounts:
Core Edition, Advanced Edition, Lock and Publish, Enterprise Edition, Enterprise 2.0 Edition, or Reseller Edition.
<br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr sz=&quot;2200&quot; b=&quot;0&quot; i=&quot;0&quot;&gt;&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;&lt;a:latin typeface=&quot;+mn-lt&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:ea typeface=&quot;+mn-ea&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:cs typeface=&quot;+mn-cs&quot;/&gt;&lt;a:sym typeface=&quot;Helvetica Neue&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:rPr&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />Please note:
On-Your-Behalf (OYB) accounts are not supported, as those are view only accounts.
And lastly, the appropriate Business Rules are required to be set up in your Salesforce Marketing Cloud account.
If you have any questions around the business rules or need it turned on, please contact your Salesforce Marketing Cloud Account Executive to enable Salesforce integration for your Marketing Cloud account.
Now let’s get started!
{}Tracking User Setup{}
The first step in setting up your Marketing Cloud Connector is to create a new tracking user.
This step enables communication between the Salesforce Marketing Cloud and Salesforce.com environments, creating a “handshake” between them.
It is recommended that the Tracking User is a system user.
First Login to Salesforce.com
<font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}Animation 1:{}

{}Animation 3:{}
Under Manage Users select Users and New User.
{}Animation 4:{}
This will bring up the New User creation page.
{}Animation 5:{}
You’ll want to select the Appropriate Role, ensure the <km val="0"><size val="2400"><strike val="noStrike"><cap val="none"><spc val="0"><normh val="0"><ln val="&lt;a:ln&gt;&lt;a:noFill/&gt;&lt;/a:ln&gt;"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><fill-uf val="&lt;a:uFillTx/&gt;"><font sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">User License is set to Salesforce and e</font></fill-uf></eff-l></ln></normh></spc></cap></strike></size></km>nsure the new Tracking User’s profile is set to System Administrator

{}Installation{}
Now that you have set up your tracking user, you can now install the Marketing Cloud Connector.
You can find the link to the install package at help.exacttarget.com under Salesforce Marketing Cloud Connector Install Guide and v5 Package Installation.
<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:srgbClr val=&quot;000000&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">{}Animation 1 {}Copy and paste the most updated version into your browser.
</font></fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:sysClr val=&quot;windowText&quot; lastClr=&quot;000000&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" sym="&lt;sym val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:sym typeface=&amp;quot;Helvetica Neue&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">This link will have you enter your Salesforce.com account credentials that you are integrating.</font></fill-sd>
{}Animation 2 {}Upon entering your credentials, it will bring you to the Package Upgrade Details Page.

{}Animation 3:{}

{}Installation{}
You will then be prompted to approve Third-Party Access.
{}Animation 1 {}Check the box to grant access and click continue
{}Animation 2 {}This will bring you to the first page of the installation process where you will need to approve the Package API access….
{}Animation 3: {}….click next
{}Animation 4:{}
The second step is to choose the security level.
The security level will depend on your security preference.
You can grant access to admins only and this will only allow you and users with your profile full access to the integration.
This is best for limited deployments.
Granting access to all users means all internal custom profiles will get full access.
Select Security settings is recommended for most packages and grants users access set by each profile.
{}Animation 5:{}
Select the Security Level that suits your needs
{}Animation 6: {}and{} {}click next
You are now ready to install your package!
This may take a while to install but you will receive an email when the installation is complete.

While the package is installing you can go ahead and add IP addresses to trusted IP ranges in order for your Marketing Cloud and Salesforce accounts to accept the calls.

{}Animation 1 {}Once in setup, you’ll need to navigate to Administer portion and select Network Access under Security Controls.

{}Edit User Page Layout{}
You will want to take the time to make sure your pages include everything we need to support the integration.
To do this you’ll navigate back to Setup and select Customize.
{}Animation 1 {}…Under the Users category, you’ll select the Page Layouts option.
{}Animation 2 {}Once in the User Page Layout screen…..
{}Animation 3: {}….you’ll want to click Edit under User Page Layouts
{}Animation 4:{}
This will bring you to the page where you can select the fields you can enter into the User Page Layout.
{}Animation 5 {}Select Marketing Cloud for AppExchange User and Marketing Cloud for AppExchange Admin
{}Animation 6 {}… and drag them onto the highlighted Additional Information Space.
Make sure you save this user layout
Note: if you are not the admin you will not need to drag the Marketing Cloud for AppExchange Admin Field
{}Enable the Marketing Cloud Connector for Admin User{}
Now that we have added these additional information fields let’s go back to the account that you are logged in as that has a System Administrator Profile.
Under Manage Users in the setup area, click users and click the desired user you need to edit.
{}Animation 1 {}Once in the User Edit screen, you’ll need to scroll down to Additional Information and Select Marketing Cloud for AppExchange User and Marketing Cloud for App Exchange Admin since we will be doing our testing through this account and will need both permissions.
Repeat this process to enable all of the users you need to integrate.
For admins select both options and for General users, select only Marketing Cloud for AppExchange User.
Be sure to click save.
