{}Customize Contact & Lead Fields{}
The next step is to set the Email Opt Out Field-Level security of your Contacts and Leads.
You’ll need to customize the Email Opt Out Field-Level Security to control the access that user profiles have.
You can choose between visible or read only or both for your users.
To set your field level security, in the App Setup section you’ll want to select Fields from the Contacts menu.
{}Animation 1:{}
You will need to select the Email Opt Out option in the Contacts Standard Fields because this is the field that requires visible level of security
{}Animation 2:{}
This will bring you to the Email Opt Out edit page
{}Animation 3:{}
From this screen you will be able to set your Field Level Security by selecting the Set Field-Level security button.
{}Animation 4:{}
Here you will be able to select what salesforce.com user profiles can have access to the field and pick between read-only and visible.
You will want to make sure that the appropriate user profiles in your organization have access to the field, especially the users who have been granted access to the Salesforce Marketing Cloud Connector.
You will also need to repeat the same process for Lead Fields.
Find Lead under Build, Select Customize, Leads and Fields then choose Email Opt out.
{}Create a Scheduled Send Workflow in Salesforce{}
Now that all of your layouts have been customized, let’s finish up the installation with setting up your workflows.
Workflows rules are critical to any organization because they give you the ability to enforce key business processes easily without having to write code.
In this case our workflows will enforce rules for our Email Send process.
To create workflows, while still in the App Setup portion in Setup and….
{}Animation 1:{}
Select Workflow Rules Under Create select Workflow & Approvals
{}Animation 2:{}
From here you will want to select the New Rule button to create the workflow.
{}Animation 3:{}
This will bring you to the first step in creating the workflow.
{}Animation 4:{}
You will need to select Email Send as the object for the workflow because this is object we want to automate.
Click Next
{}Animation 5:{}
In step 2, you will select the parameters for the workflow rule.
{}Animation 6:{}
Enter the rule name of ScheduledSend, with no spaces and must be typed exactly like this
{}Animation 7:{}
Next, select the Evaluation Criteria option of created.
{}Animation 8:{}
Finally, make sure that the “Run this rule if the following” drop down is set to “criteria are met” and the Field drop down is set to you “Email Send:
Scheduled Date/Time,” the operator is set to “not equal to” and the value field is blank.
{}Animation 9:{}
Once your parameters are set, Click Save and Next
{}Adding Time Triggers{}
Step 3 of creating the workflow requires you to specify a time trigger.
{}Animation 1:{}
Click {}Add Time Trigger {}under {}Time-Dependent Workflow Actions{}
{}Animation 2:{}
This will allow you to create the time trigger.
Ensure that the workflow rule is set to 0 Hours After Email Send Scheduled Date/Time and click save
{}Adding a Field Update & Activate{}
We now need to add a Field Update to our Time Dependent Workflow Action we just created.
A Field update is an action that is associated with a workflow rule.
In this case we are using the action DelayedSend.
To start adding a field update we need to select an existing action to update.
{}Animation 1:{}
This can be found under the Time Dependent Workflow Action we just created
{}Animation 2: {}in the Add Workflow Action Dropdown menu. Select, select existing action
{}Animation 3:{}
This will bring you to an edit page where you will be able to select your action.
{}Animation 4:{}
For the Search drop down, select Field Update
{}Animation 5:{}
Then move Field Update: DelayedSend from Available actions to Selected Actions by clicking the Add arrow so that your selection looks it does on the screen shot.
{}Animation 6:{}
Click Save and then Done.
{}Animation 7:{}
The final set is to make sure you activate your Rule by clicking Activate.
Once you click Activate, choose a Default Workflow User (Preferably an Admin), click save, the button will change to Deactivate and you will see a checkmark to acknowledge the rule is activated
You will need to create one more workflow rule using the same process.
This workflow rule will use the same object, Email Send, and be titled BackupWorkflow (with no spaces & exactly like this) and will be necessary to backup your Email Sends automatically.
Set the Evaluation Criteria to Evaluate the rule when a record is: Created, and any time it’s edited to subsequently meet criteria.
Run this rule when “Criteria are Met” and enter the following Rule Criteria Email Send: Backup Workflow Date/Time not equal to (blank).
Add the time trigger Set this Workflow Rule to 0 Hours After Email Send: Backup Workflow Date/Time and add the Field Update: UnpopulateBackupWorkflow.
Make sure to click Activate and you are finished creating your workflows!
{}User Configuration in the Marketing Cloud{}
Now that we’ve concurred the installation let’s make sure that our Salesforce account is configured with our Marketing Cloud account
{}Set Salesforce Tracking User in the Marketing Cloud{}
Our next step is to integrate our Marketing Cloud users with the salesforce.com users.
Remember, there is a one-to-one relationship for this, meaning that one Marketing Cloud user is associated with one salesforce.com User.
To do so we will need to log into our Marketing Cloud account we set up in the first webinar of this series.
{}Animation 1:{}
In the Admin tab, you will select the Salesforce Integration option from the left navigation.
{}Animation 2:{}
Next you will need to add your Tracking User Name and Password you set up within salesforce.com in the Configurations Settings in the workspace so that the Marketing Cloud can complete the handshake.
{}Animation 3:{}
Once you have entered this information, your Salesforce Org ID should populate.
If it does not, you must use the magnifying glass to search for an Org ID
You have the option of selecting Scope By User here.
Let’s dive in next on whether this option might be useful for you…
{}Scope By User vs Non-Scope By User{}
{}Scope By User{}
{}Non Scope By User{}
Limited to what is visible by the user initiating the send
Not limited to what is visible to the user initiating the send
Works well if migrating from v3 to v5 integrations
Works well if migrating from v2 to v5 integrations
User must enter their Salesforce password
An admin can set up a user without entering a password
When user’s password expires, that user must update their Salesforce password in the Marketing Cloud
Passwords do not expire
{}With a Scope By User configuration{}, Reports and Campaign that are visible to the user initiating the send are available for this selection within the Salesforce Marketing Cloud as a target audience for reports and campaigns.
Subscribers are filtered based on the user initiating the send.
The list of Subscribers returned is limited to what the user initiating the send has access to view.
{}For a Scope By User configuration you may want to consider a few things.{}
Within the Salesforce Marketing Cloud, Report and/or Campaign lists are limited to what is visible by the user initiating the send.
The send behavior described above is the default behavior for SFv3 accounts, making this a favorable option of existing SFv3 customers who wish to migrate to SFv5
Users must enter their Salesforce password during the integration User process in the Salesforce Marketing Cloud
When a user’s Salesforce password expires, that user must update their Salesforce password on the Salesforce Marketing Cloud
{}With a Non- Scope By User configuration{}, Subscribers who are visible or accessible to the Tracking User can be retrieved from reports or campaigns.
Often, the Tracking User is an Administrator within Salesforce with wide-ranging access.
Thus, the list of subscribers returned from each report or campaign includes all subscribers visible to this user.
Subscribers are not filtered based on the user running the report which is the biggest difference between the two configuration options.
{}For a Non-Scope By User configuration you may want to consider a few things.{}
The send behavior described above is the default for SFv2 accounts, making this a favorable option for existing SFv2 customers who wish to migrate to SFv5
Within the Salesforce Marketing Cloud, Report and/or Campaign lists are not limited to what is visible to the user initiated send
Within the Salesforce Marketing Cloud, returned Subscribers are not limited to only those visible to the user initiating the send
Password policies are not in effect, making this configuration easy to maintain because passwords do not expire
An Administrator can set up a user without entering a password
A potential risk would be if a user could mistakenly sends to a Report and/or Campaign members who are not visible to that user without notice.
This is the biggest difference between the two configurations.
{}Please refer to the workbook for more review of which configuration would work best for your account{}

Integrate User First
There are slightly different steps to manage different types of users.
As mentioned before, a user can either be a Scope By User or a Non Scope By User.
There are different account types as well including Enterprise 2.0 and Non Enterprise 2.0.
To help break this down, please refer to the flow chart.
{}If you have an Enterprise 2.0 account with Scope By User configuration {}you will need to manage your Business Units and give minimum permissions including Content Creator and Marketing Cloud Viewer.
A Content Creator role can access all facets of content creation, but they have no control over other aspects of the Salesforce Marketing Cloud application such as subscriber information and tracking results.
This user produces the images and words that will be used in the actual messages which are then approved and sent by other roles.
The Marketing Cloud viewer permission allows the user to view messages in the Marketing Cloud.
{}For an Enterprise 2.0 account with a Non Scope By User configuration{}, you will need to again manage your Business Units as well as set minimum permissions.
These include Content Creator the same role as before but two additional permissions; Data Manager and Marketing Cloud Content Editor/Publisher.
The data manager role  allows the user to maintain subscriber records and any publication or suppression lists and handles data imports and exports.
The database marketer may have to create relationships that span multiple business units, but this role usually doesn’t create or edit the content itself.
The Marketing Cloud Content Editor/ Publisher allows the user to edit and publish content.
{}If you account is a Non Enterprise 2.0 account{}, it’s time to listen up!
A scope by user will need to set the following permissions:
Content Creator and Marketing Viewer.
These are the same permissions as an Enterprise 2.0 account scope by user.
{}If your account is a Non Enterprise 2.0 account and you have a non scope by user {}you need to integrate, you may need to go about it a slightly different way than the others types.
The Manage Roles button is not active in the Salesforce Marketing Cloud Core and Enterprise 1.0 account.
So in this case you will need to scroll down in the edit user record screen to Permissions and Roles and select the following:
Grant the user access to the web service which will allow the user to create web service API calls for the Salesforce Marketing Cloud system to process.
Manage Data Extension Data and Retention Policy to allow the user to set their account’s data retention policy and
Administrative Data Management to access the data retention policies for data extensions and also allow access to Manage Salesforce Data features to delete data stored in the Salesforce Database
We will go into detail of how to set up these users next.
{}Manage Roles & Business Units<br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />Non Scope by User- Enterprise 2.0 Account{}

Content Creator, Data Manager and Marketing Cloud Content Editor/Publisher
Repeat this process for all integration users
{}Manage Roles<br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />Non Scope by User – Core and Enterprise 1.0 Accounts{}

{}Selecting Triggered Sends{}
{}Speaker1 {}Now that we have set up our tabs we will need to complete some prerequisites before configuring the Marketing Cloud with our Salesforce account.
We need to set up a small APEX code in order for our two instances to “talk” to each other.
This will affect the triggers that we will create.
Triggered Email Sends allows Marketing Cloud Connector customers to create and send automated messages to Salesforce contact, lead or person account records when object records are created and/or updated.
In order to create a trigger you must set up a small APEX code for each object you plan on using as a trigger.
Let’s get into how we are going to set this up…
{}Animation 1:{}
In Salesforce, under setup select customize where you will find a list of objects that you can set up as triggers.
{}Animation 2:{}
For this example we are choosing the object, Lead.
{}Animation 3:{}
Under Lead select Triggers
{}Animation 4:{}
Here you can select New and we can enter an APEX code that will connect our trigger.
{}Animation 5:{}
This will bring up Apex Trigger Editing Screen
{}Animation 6:{}
First you’ll want to make sure your Apex trigger is active, so be sure to check the Is Active box
{}Animation 7:{}
Next you’ll want to enter in the code shown in the editing box exactly how it is and change the object for each additional apex trigger you create.
In this case you would swap out the word Lead for a different object.
You can copy and paste this code from help.exacttarget.com and searching Triggered Sends.
You can also find out more about triggered sends there as well.
*** I am not able to find the apex code in help, so not sure if that language needs to be removed or the link to take you there.
If it is there, not easy to find.
*** Also, when I enter the code above, I get an error that I am not able to figure out.
{}Animation 8:{}
Click Save when you are finished and repeat this process for every object you plan on using a trigger for

{}Speaker1 {}Next you’ll need to choose your restrictions for triggered sends.
{}Animation 1 {}You can allow only administrators or both admins and standard users to create triggered sends

The option to cancel the send will stop it form be retried further
{}Animation 5 {}You’ll need to choose the tracking level preferences.
There are 4 different forms of tracking details that you can choose from.
{}Aggregate Level Tracking {}provides a comprehensive summary of Email Send statistics.
This can viewed graphically in the Tracking Info section of the Email Send record.
{}Individual Level Tracking{} provides email performance tracking information down to the Contact or Lead Level.
They can be viewed in the Individual Email Result record which is accessible from the Related List on the Email Send record or from Contact or Lead record.
{}Track Link Details{} allows individual subscriber link tracking data such as links clicked or number of clicks to be stored in Salesforce.
This consumes additional Salesforce storage.
This preference provides Link Tracking information for each individual Lead or Contact that is part of a send.
{}Track Sent Events{} stores Individual Subscriber-level tracking data in Salesforce after an email is sent.
If this option is not selected, this data is stored in Salesforce only after a subscriber takes action such as opening an email or clicking a link.
This tracking option may consume a large amount of data.
{}Animation 6 {}You can change the frequency  that you will receive tracking
{}Animation 7 {}and change the number of days to track

{}Business Units{}
A business unit allows you to control your brand while enabling access to messaging technologies.
A parent/child structure
Can be organized in any way to support your business
Can limit data visible to business units (i.e. AMER only sees AMER subscribers, APAC only sees APAC subscribers)
Now that we’ve set up the account settings, let’s talk about business units and reasons why you might use them for your organization.
Business units allow you to control data for purposes such as branding and regulatory compliance for direct email marketing campaigns but still provide access to the Marketing Cloud to other areas of your organization.
It is important to point out that business units are implemented in a hierarchical, parent/child structure.
A business unit is a hierarchical administration structure that controls access to information and sharing of information.
All items created in a business unit are accessible to all users working in that business unit.
Items can be shared with other users in other business units by placing them into a shared items folder, located in the Content and Subscriber sections of the applications.
Business units can also manage the visibility of data within an account using a hierarchical structure, which can be organized in any way to match your business needs.
When setting up your business units you can mirror workflow processes, demographic and behavioral data about your subscribers, or your organization's operational structure – which ever works best for you organization.
As an administrator, a business unit also allows you to manage user roles for the business unit, view users who have access to the business unit, and define filter criteria for subscribers.
{}Creating a Business Unit{}
Creating Business Units is easy in your Marketing Cloud account!
{}Animation 1:{}
To begin creating a business unit navigate to the {}Admin {}tab in your account and click {}Business Units.{}
{}Animation 2:{}
From the toolbar within the Business Unit workspace click the {}create {}button.
This will open up the {}New Business Unit{} workspace where you will complete the {}Properties {}section and the {}Physical Address{} section.
Depending on how you are setting up your business units, you may need to have a different physical address than your Parent business unit.
For example, if you are setting up your business units based on country that your organization has office in and you want the physical address to be the office in that country.
The next section you will need to complete is the {}Unsubscribe Settings{} sections.
As an Enterprise 2.0 administrator you can manage how business unit level unsubscribes are handled and ensure it works best for your organization.
Two options are available under the properties settings of a business unit:
Subscribers will be unsubscribed from all business units in the Enterprise
Subscribers will be unsubscribed from this business unit only
If you pick the “Subscribers will be unsubscribed from all business units in the Enterprise” option the following will happen:
When a subscriber is unsubscribed in All subscribers from a business unit, the subscriber is unsubscribed in the All Subscriber list at the enterprise level.
Activating a subscriber in All Subscribers list at business unit level does not activate the subscriber at the business unit level.
This is because the subscriber is unsubscribed in the All Subscriber list at the enterprise level (master unsubscribed) and that trumps the business unit level.
Activating the subscriber in All Subscribers at the enterprise level does not activate the subscriber at the business unit level.
This is because the subscriber is unsubscribed in the All Subscriber list at the business unit level.
In order for a subscriber to be reactivated the subscriber must be activated at the enterprise and business unit levels.
If you pick the “Subscribers will be unsubscribed from this business unit only.” option the following will happen:
Unsubscribing a subscriber in All Subscribers at business unit level does not unsubscribe the subscriber in the All Subscriber list at the enterprise level.
Activating the subscriber in the All Subscrbers list at the business unit level activates the subscriber at the business unit level.

{}CAN-SPAM{}
The CAN-SPAM (Controlling the Assault of Non-Solicited Pornography and Marketing) Act is the U.S. Federal standards for the sending of email messages.
There are two classifications of emails:
Commercial: the primary purpose is to deliver commercial content.
Must include the physical mailing address and opt-out mechanism
Transactional: primary purpose is to communicate transactional content.
No unsubscribe link required.
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
Before we configure the Send Classification, let’s talk about the Controlling the Assault of Non-Solicited Pornography and Marketing Act, or the CAN-SPAM Act as most of us know it, that is the US federal standards.
There are 2 classifications of emails based on the act:
Commercial emails are when the primary purpose of the message is to deliver commercial content.
Examples include newsletters, weekly specials, upcoming events, etc.
Commercial emails MUST include your physical mailing address and provide an opt-out/unsubscribe mechanism.
Transactional emails are normally initiated by the subscriber.
Examples include order confirmations, shipping notices, thank you emails, etc.
An unsubscribe link is not required in transactional messages.
Remaining in compliance with the CAN-SPAM Act is very important as non-compliance can lead to fines, litigation, even imprisonment.
If you are unsure if an email is commercial or transactional, we recommend you include the unsubscribe link though that is not legal advice.
If you do have questions about your emails and CAN-SPAM, we recommend you engage your legal counsel for details specific to your organization.
{}Send Classification{}
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
Now that we’ve created a sender profile and a delivery profile, you are able to configure a send classification.
A send classification allows you to define parameters for email jobs in a central location to save time and effort, mitigate risk and give you greater control of sends in your account.
The send classification will specify the sender profile, delivery profile, and the CAN-SPAM classification.
To create a send classification, click create from the toolbar and
{}Animation 1: {}…Give it a name, but the external key, and description are again optional.
{}Animation 2:{}
Next you will set the CAN-SPAM classification – commercial or transactional.
{}Animation 3:{}
Then identify the appropriate sender and delivery profile that were created in the previous 2 steps.
{}Animation 4:{}
You also have the opportunity to select a send priority and it will set the priority of which the email is sent.
Normal is the default and the email will be sent at a normal pace.
Low will result in the send being given a lower priority and may take longer than normal to complete the send.
High, which may not be enabled in your account, will result in the email send being given priority over other sends in the account.
{}Animation 5:{}
The final step is to save the send classification you’ve created.

{}BrandBuilder{}
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Speaker 2:{}
The last section we will cover today is the BrandBuilder.
The BrandBuilder is a private labeling tool that allows you to provide a branded experience to both your application users and your subscribers by configuring certain aspects, including:

{}SUBSCRIBERS RULE!{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
We have a lot of information to cover today so let’s get started with the SUBSCRIBERS RULE!
Philosophy, it will help set the groundwork for subscriber management.
{}SUBSCRIBERS RULE!{}
Serve the individual.
Honor their unique preference with regard to communication, <br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />content, frequency & channels.
Deliver to them timely, relevant content that improves their lives.
{}Speaker 1:{}
The first step to achieving success with your email marketing is understanding the industry’s best practices.
The SUBSCRIBERS RULE philosophy will help you gain that understanding and start you on the path to success.
It is based on three tenets:
Serve the individual
Honor their unique preferences with regard to communication, content, frequency, and channels.
Deliver timely, relevant content that improves their lives.
Basically, your subscribers come first, so you want to ensure you respect their preferences and deliver relevant content to them with every communication you send.

Email Address - which is a require attribute in the account and cannot be removed ,
User defined - is a generic attribute which you may use however you wish, and
Full name - which can be deleted along with the user define attribute if you choose to do so

1.

2.
Tab Delimited or
3.
Other Delimited, where the delimiter can be pipes or another of your choosing
Finally you have the update options – your selection here may vary depending on if it is new list or a list you are updating.
Your options include:
1.
Add new subscribers and update subscribers who already exist; which will both add and update your subscribers.
This option is most suitable for the majority of your import scenarios.
2.
Add new subscribers but do not update subscribers who already exist; will only add new subscribers – existing subscribers will not be modified.
3.
Update existing subscribers but do not add subscribers that do not exist; it will only update subscribers who are already present in the list and will not import new subscribers.

{}Groups{}
Now that we have subscribers in lists, let’s discuss how you can further segment your lists to drive relevant communications.
{}What is a Group?{}
A group is a subset of subscribers from a list (or another group).
Allows you to make targeted lists of subscribers at random or based on specific criteria.
Speaker 1:
<size val="2400"><kern val="1200"><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx2&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">Groups are a subset of subscribers they allow you to create a targeted selection of subscribers based on random or specified criteria.
Groups can be created from lists, or even other groups within the application.</font></eff-l></fill-sd></kern></size>
{}Group Creation Options{}
There are two methods to create a group.
Filtered:
Create a group based on criteria about the subscriber.
Random:
Create a group with subscribers either randomly selected or selected at a fixed interval.
Speaker 1:
There are two methods of group creation:
Filtered groups allows you to build a rule that is based on profile and preferences attributes.
Filtered groups also allow you to build groups based on a data filter, which uses the same creation method as a filter.
We are not coving data filters today, however you can get further information on data filters at help.exacttarget.com.
Random groups allow you to pick a random group of subscribers by specifying the number of subscribers or percentage of the list that should be used.
You can also create a random group using a fixed interval that allows you to specify the number of subscribers you want in your group and at what interval they should be chosen.
You can create up to 12 groups for each list or group in the application, and up to 12 groups can be created at once using certain methods.
The method you choose will vary depending on the intention for the group.
For example, are you creating groups for segmentation?
If you are, a filtered group is likely the group you’d use.
Are you creating the group for testing?
If yes, you’ll likely create a group using the random method.
Let take a better look at each of these methods…
{}Filtered Group Creation{}
Speaker 1:
To create a filtered group navigate to My Groups and
{}Animation 1: {}click Create.
{}Animation 2:{}
Choose the Filtered Group option.
{}Animation 3:{}
Next, you will indicate the source the group will be derived from.
This will be the list that will provide the population from which your group is created.
You can pick either a list you’ve created in your account, the All Subscribers list that holds all subscribers in your account, or another group.
{}Filtered Group Creation{}
Speaker 1:
Next you will select the Profile or Preference attributes and set values.
{}Animation 1:{}
Here you can drag and drop attributes onto the Create Filter Canvas and configure each attribute to the conditions you need for your group creation.
{}Animation 2:{}
In the drop down, you will see that the email application has quite a few predefined functions that you can use when creating your group.
{}Animation 3:{}
You can also change the and/or operators by hovering over the bottom of the or/and box and drag it up or down according to the range you would like to cover.
{}Animation 4:{}
When you have all your conditions set, click save & build.
{}Animation 5:{}
The final step is to provide a name for your group, a description if needed, and determine the location you would like your group to be saved in.
By default, the group will be saved in the My Groups folder.
Once you click save, the email application will build your group!
{}Live Demonstration:<br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" /><size val="3600">{}Creating a Filtered Group</size>{}{}
Now let’s take a look at this feature in a live environment, give me just a moment to set this up.

{}Portfolio{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
Our first area of focus will be on Portfolio, which is our first step in preparation to create our email.
{}Portfolio{}
Manage your email send assets online, including images, documents, and media files.
{}Speaker 1:{}
What is Portfolio?
Portfolio allows you to manage your email assets online.
You can store a wide variety of files in Portfolio including images, documents, and media files to be used in an email.
All common file types are supported for images & graphics, documents, text, office files, and audio & video files.
Images uploaded to Portfolio can be up to 200KB each – this size should be sufficient for your image uploads as they will be resized for inclusion in your email.
All other file types – i.e. documents, multimedia – can be up to 1MB each.
If you ever encounter an issue with the size limitation or require an item to be added which exceeds the sizes noted, please contact Global Support for assistance.
File names must be at least 5 characters long as well.
{}Portfolio Upload Options{}
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
There are 2 options for uploading items into Portfolio.
Single Upload and
Batch upload
Lets take a closer look at the steps for each of these options….
{}Animation 1:{}
Clicking the single upload option from the Portfolio navigation bar will begin the process…..
{}Animation 2:{}
The wizard will open to allow you to upload a file.
Choose your file by first clicking the browse button.
Once the file is chosen, give it a unique file name, though the external key and description are optional.
Click Ok to start the uploading process.
{}Animation 3:{}
Clicking the batch upload option will allow you to upload multiple files at the same time.
Those files are also required to be in a zipped folder first.
{}Animation 4:{}
The wizard opens to begin that process.
Just as with the single option, you will click browse and select the zipped folder you want to upload into Portfolio.
If you accidentally added a file to that folder you don’t want uploaded into Portfolio, you have the opportunity to erase it by clicking the Remove hyperlink before uploading your files.
Just as with the single option, click Ok to begin the upload process.
Batch upload is a great option if you have a lot of files to import at once.
{}Portfolio Management{}
Portfolio Items can be deleted, moved to another folder, properties reviewed/updated, and previewed.
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
Once you have your portfolio items uploaded in the application they can be easily managed.
Any item no longer required can be removed by selecting the item(s) and clicking delete.
If you need to move an item to another folder, choose that file and click move.
A select folder dialogue box will open allowing you to pick the appropriate folder.
Item properties can be viewed or modified at any time as well – simply select the item and click properties.
Here are some general recommendations to help you get the most out of Portfolio.
Leverage folders to organize your Portfolio items.
You can create folders for different emails, campaigns, item type and so on, to suit your preferences.
There is an exercise in your Workbook to outline a folder structure that will work best for you.
Ensure each file has a unique name when they share the same extension and a unique external key.
When an item is uploaded, by default, the file name minus the file extension will be the name of the file.
You can upload a file with the same name and different extension, but the external key is required to be unique.
Duplicate file names with the same extension or external keys will cause an error during the upload process, just change the name or external key to fix that issue.
Optimize images by resizing them to the desired pixel width and height prior to uploading them into Portfolio.
While you can resize images within Portfolio, you’ll have the best results using an image editor like adobe to resize them before the upload.
Also, as a best practice – images being used as a header in an email should be 600 X 150 pixels, as that is the exact size of the template header area.
{}Templates{}
{}Speaker 2:{}
We begin to use our portfolio items in the next step – which is creating Templates.
Templates are used to control the header, background color, borders, and content layout of an email.
They allow you to brand your email and create consistent layouts for your subscribers.
There are a number of advantages of using templates including consistency in branding and layouts.
Templates make it easy for non-technical users to create emails, and the templates themselves.
Content creation and template creation can be completed by 2 different users – i.e. a graphic designer manages the templates and a copywriter populates content in the email.
{}Creating Templates{}

There are 2 options to create a template – using the template editor and pasting in your own HTML.
The template editor allows you to pick from 13 mobile optimized layouts and 7 static predefined layouts that can be used without any indebt technical knowledge of creating emails.
Paste HTML allows you to take advantage of the power of customized HTML coding while providing users with a graphical user interface and content boxes it can be used in.
We’ll take a look at the steps required for both options.
First we’ll walk through creating a template using the Template editor.

By default, the template will be placed in the My Templates folder.
Finally, the default Template Source is “User Template Editor”, we will leave that radio button selected and click save in the toolbar.
{}Template Editor{}
The template editor will guide you through how you can make the template consistent with your brand’s look and feel.
Best Practice: headers should be image only (maximum width 600 pixels).
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Speaker 2:{}
Our template has now been created and notice it is a blank template.

Then save the Header which will take us back to the Template Editor screen where we will see the header displayed.

{}Paste HTML Template{}
Create the HTML in a third party editor.
Copy & Paste the HTML code into Marketing Cloud
Preview/Test template as needed.
Insert the email open tracking and Save.
{}Speaker 1:{}
You can also create your template by pasting your own HTML into the application.
If you are going to use this option there are a few things to remember:
You can create the HTML using the HTML editor of your choice, such as Dreamweaver or Notepad
There are a few items you may need to included in your code
The Email open tracking code – Needed to get your opens in tracking
Code to create content areas – For easy editing in the email and to add a marketing cloud survey
Tracking alias for links – Which will be the name of the link in tracking
CAN-SPAM compliance components – This is optional according to your account setup, ie, you requested changes in your default footer
Personalization strings – Also optional, only add them if needed
{}Code to Include in Paste HTML Template{}
Email Open Tracking Code
{}<custom name = "opencounter" type = "tracking">{}
Content Area Code
{}<custom type="content" name="[Content Name]">{}
Tracking Alias
{}<a href = “http://www.salesforce.com/marketing-cloud/overview/” alias = “Salesforce Marketing Cloud Homepage Header”>{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
I want to spend a few minutes providing some more information on the additional code that we just spoke about;
{}Email Open Tracking Code:{}
The email open tracking code is what allows you to track opens within the Salesforce Marketing Cloud.
The code shown on the screen inserts a 1x1 transparent GIF that when images are enabled, the open is captured.
For best results, place the email open tracking code at the top or bottom outside of your <body> tags, because certain email clients will not render all images in an email until the subscriber scrolls.
If the email open tracking code is not included in your code, the Salesforce Marketing Cloud will warn you that it is missing when saving your template.
And if the email is sent without the code, the opens are not able to be captured.
{}Content Area Code:{}
The content area code provides editable regions within the email that users can populate with images, text, or both during the email creation process.
It is also required if you plan to add a Marking Cloud survey in your email, as they are in form format.
It is recommended that you include content areas within a <td> or <tr> tag and important to note that each content area requires a unique name, which can be used to provide guidance on what type of content should be included within the content area.
For example, we see many customers give content areas names like Hero Image, Header, Preheader, Main Article or Body.
{}Tracking Alias:{}
If you are going to be including the same link in multiple places within an email, you will want to provide an alias for tracking purposes.
We will cover tracking more in-depth in a future session, but click tracking is done at the alias level within the application.
By using an alias, you will be able to differentiate between the subscribers that clicked each link, when the same link is used in the email.
Tracking aliases also make it easier to read the tracking overview when using a descriptive alias, for example, using Salesforce Marketing Cloud  Header vs. using just Salesforce Marketing Cloud.
Another important item to note is when an alias isn’t provided, the alias will default to the URL.
If the same URL is in numerous places, you will lose the visibility into which of the links got the most click activity within tracking.

Once you’ve created your template, test it to ensure it is rendering as you expected!
If you have tools such as Litmus or Return Path available to you, they can help you understand how the template is rendering across numerous email clients and browsers at once.

{}Adding Content{}
IN APPLICATION

{}Adding Content – Smart Orientation{}
IN APPLICATION
This will open the Content Building Wizard.
The first step in the wizard is to select a Smart Orientation which allows you to easily configure the content area.
There are eight options here, most are self-explanatory:
Text Only or Image Only will only support the option selected
You can select an orientation with both text and image that has the image confined to a specific location within the content area – top, bottom, left or right.
Free form is the most flexible option allowing you to add images, text and tables to the Content area.
By using this option you can add multiple images to your content box, text where ever you like and even custom html.
The final option is HTML Only.
If you intend to paste custom HTML created outside the application and edit it in html only mode, then this is the best option.
{}Adding Content{}

{}Personalization{}
To add to a content area select the Personalization drop down and select an attribute.
To add to the email subject click the Personalization icon and select the attribute.
IN APPLICATION
Subject lines and Content areas that include text can include personalization.
Personalization allows you to create customized content for your subscriber based on attributes populated in the Salesforce Marketing Cloud or your instance of Salesforce.com if you are using the Marketing Cloud Connector–attributes were covered in the adding subscribers webinar.
For some context, you can use personalization to include the subscriber’s first name in an email, so it is personalize for each subscriber.
To add personalization to the text of a content area, first place the cursor where you would like the field to be added, then click the Personalization drop down and select the attribute to include.
This will populate that personalization string where you have indicated in the text.
You can also add personalization to an email subject line by selecting the personalization icon next to the subject field.
Again, we will select the attribute to add.
Personalization can also be typed directly into the email subject line or content area by including two sets of percentage signs around the attribute, for example,  %%First_Name%%.
A few important items to note when it comes to personalization:
Personalization strings are space sensitive.
Always remember to include a space before and after the string if needed.
If a value for the attribute is empty, a null or blank value will appear in the email.
Ensure a default value is used for attributes to avoid this, such as ‘Valued Customer’ for first name.
{}Links{}
IN APPLICATION
Another common practice is to include links in your email.
There are many ways links can be used – we can link to additional information to keep our email concise, link to landing pages or microsites for subscribers to complete Smart Capture forms, and there are other opportunities for links as well.
Inserting links is simple, just highlight the text or image you would like to link to and
{}Animation 1:{}
Choose hyperlink from the Insert dropdown.
{}Animation 2:{}
Or you can click on the hyperlink icon as well.
<size val="2400">{}Animation 3:{}
E</size><size val="2000">ither option will open the Insert Link wizard.
In the Link To field you can leave the default of website and enter a URL to link to.
Or if you click the dropdown by website, you can choose one of the other options.
For now we will focus on linking to a website so you will want to enter the URL to link to.
Below the URL field there could be an option for Conversion Tracking List, it is not available in all accounts.
Conversion tracking allows you to track the number of click throughs for a link and even compare performance on links in an email.
To activate conversion tracking, check this option.</size>
In the Link Display area, we have two fields which will both default to the highlighted text.
First, the Link Tooltip, which is also optional – it will display when a subscriber hovers over the link.
You may choose to modify this to something more descriptive – such as the actual webpage name or a call to action, like Complete loyalty profile
The second field is the Tracking Alias which is a required field – use this field to specify the link name for tracking.
You may include the same link multiple times in an email, such as a link to your company’s website.
By default, tracking will aggregate all of those clicks into one, which is great for getting an overall number.
But if you would like the performance of each link separately, assign each link a unique tracking alias.

{}Creating an email using HTML Paste{}
IN APPLICATION
You also have the option of creating an HTML paste email.
If you choose this option, you will not use the templates available in your account but will instead use HTML code.
You can either create HTML code directly in the application or paste HTML from an external editor.
To create an email this way you will go to the Create button in the My Emails toolbar and select HTML Paste.
{}Animation 1:{}
You will then be on the properties page for your email where you will provide a name for it – remember this isn’t visible to subscribers.
Though the subject line for the email is, also the preheader if one is being used and select the location you wish to store the email.
The fields should look familiar as they are the same options when creating an email from a template.
{}Animation 2:{}
Once you complete your choices, clicking Save will save the properties and take us to the editor were we are able to view the paste html template.
{}Creating an email using HTML Paste{}
The next screen is where you can either create your HTML code within the workspace or copy and paste the HTML code from an external editor into the application.
When working with emails created with HTML code, you may need to insert certain items that are required by the federal CAN-SPAM Act.
For emails built using a standard template, these items are automatically embedded into the email.
{}Physical mailing address{}:
All commercial email must contain a physical mailing address.
You need to insert your physical mailing address using the email tools provided; it cannot be typed directly into the email.
{}Link to unsubscribe or modify profile{}:
All commercial email must contain a valid opt-out mechanism.
To meet this requirement, you can embed a link in your emails by which you can unsubscribe from your communications.
In addition, you can also give your subscribers the ability to update their profile information.
Make sure the images are uploaded in your <lnk-c val="&lt;a:hlinkClick r:id=&quot;rId3&quot; tooltip=&quot;/link/a2a08f2c6acf4a26a398bd84944d8461.aspx?id=6454&amp;amp;epslanguage=en&quot;/&gt;">Portfolio</lnk-c> folder or your company server before you create your email, as the url for them are needed to use in the code.
Also check the URLs in the email code to make sure they correspond properly.
{}Animation 1:{}

{}Content Detective{}
Content Detective helps you identify potential spam triggers in your email content
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Spearker2: (if two speakers){}
The first tool you can use is Content Detective.
This feature mirrors the logic used by spam-filtering software to identify words, phrases, image sizes and patterns that are likely to trigger filters and recommends changing the issue it fines.
If one trigger is found in your email, generally it will probably not affect deliverability.
Though it is always a great ideal to make the change because the email service providers periodically change their spam software and that word could generate a higher spam score.
However, when two or more are found it is recommended you edit your content as suggested by content detective to reduce the likelihood of the email being filtered as spam.
Content detective will not force you to make those changes, but you are taking a risk on deliverability if you do not.
To run this check, click Content Detective from the toolbar.
It will scan the entire email, including the links and their properties and any custom coding that were added.
{}Content Detective{}
Any triggers found will be listed on the results screen
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Spearker2: (if two speakers){}
If any triggers are found, both the problem and a suggested resolution will be displayed.
On the results screen you can print or save the results which is handy if someone else is responsible for the content and you are verifying prior to sending.
{}Animation 1:{}
You can edit the email to fix any problems identified by clicking the edit button.
Tip:
If it finds a word you are not able to find in the body of the email, check your link properties and or go to the html tab to check for it there.
{}Validate{}
Validating your email will check your for common issues that could prevent your email from being sent.
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Spearker2: (if two speakers){}
Next, you will want to validate your email which will scan the email for common issues that could prevent your email from being sent.
Using validation will help improve your delivery rate and help ensure the send appears to your subscribers as you intend.
It will check for:
CAN-SPAM compliance (i.e. the presence of an unsubscribe link and presence of a physical mailing address, two items that are required for commercial emails)
It will also check for correct syntax for the attribute personalization strings used in the email.
Validating your email is easy.
{}Animation 1:{}
In the email workspace, click Validate from the toolbar.
{}Animation 2:{}
Select subscriber lists or groups you want The Target of the Email Send to be validated against.
{}Animation 3:{}
Click the Validate button again.
{}Animation 4:{}
Ideally you will receive confirmation on screen that no problems were found.
If you do run into issues, you will see them outlined on this screen.
Tip:
For can-spam compliance, your template based emails will automatically have the default footer added to it, which is can-spam compliant.
But your custom html emails requires that you add it and this feature will inform you if it is not included.

{}Speaker 1:{}

{}Test Send{}

{}User Initiated Sends{}
{}Speaker 1:{}

{}What is a user initiated send?{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
A user initiated send is primarily used for sending emails via programs, or automations, in the Interaction tab.
It allows you to set the parameters for a send once, but it may be used numerous times – i.e. daily, weekly, monthly, etc.
While it is primarily used for programs, you can send an email from the user-initiated workspace in the Interactions tab.
Next we will go over how you will set up a user initiated send and how to send the email.
{}Animation 1:{}
The first step in creating a user initiated send is clicking the create button in the toolbar of the workspace.
{}Creating a User Initiated Send{}
Speaker 1:

{}Animation 2:{}

{}Animation 3:{}

{}Animation 4:{}

{}Sending using a User Initiated Send{}

{}Animation 2:{}

You can select the Start immediately, run once or the Start on the following date and time, run once option, where you can select the appropriate date and time for the email to be delivered.
Both options will only run the user initiated send once.
{}Animation 3:{}

{}Animation 4:{}

<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx1&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;Arial&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;-112&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;0&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;MS PGothic&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;34&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;-128&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;ＭＳ Ｐゴシック&amp;quot; pitchFamily=&amp;quot;-112&amp;quot; charset=&amp;quot;-128&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">We’ve covered quite a bit of territory in our journey over the last few sessions.
Today, we want to wrap this up and give you some guidance on h</font></fill-sd><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx2&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;"><eff-l val="&lt;a:effectLst/&gt;"><font latin="&lt;latin val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:latin typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-lt&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" ea="&lt;ea val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:ea typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-ea&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;" cs="&lt;cs val=&quot;&amp;lt;a:cs typeface=&amp;quot;+mn-cs&amp;quot;/&gt;&quot;&gt;">ow to leverage tracking data to obtain feedback from campaigns to improve your communications. </font></eff-l></fill-sd>
{}My Tracking{}
SUCCESS – GETTING STARTED
{}Speaker 1:{}
Let’s jump in and start getting familiar to the My Tracking section of the Salesforce Marketing Cloud.
{}Accessing Tracking{}
Tracking is an aggregated collection of data that allows you to view <br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />critical elements
{}Speaker 1:{}
All tracking and reporting items are located under the tracking tab in the email application which is broken up into three sections - my tracking, my reports and my data.
Today we will focus on my tracking and my reports.
This Tracking area of the email application is an aggregated collection of data that allows you to view critical elements for your sends.
You will be able to track various items related to your sends including the unique and total opens,, how many links were clicked (and which ones), un-deliverables, and much more.
By default, tracking data will remain in your account for the duration of your contract.
{}Note:{}
Sometimes subscribers do not receive an email, but tracking doesn't show those emails as being undeliverable.
An email is deemed delivered as long as there isn’t a bounce received.
Remember when you created your template?
If you chose to create a template using HTML Paste, you may have seen a prompt to insert the email open tracking code into the email template, if it wasn’t already in your HTML.
As the open is counted by the tracking pixel loading in your account, if a subscriber has images turned off or they are not supported in their webmail client, their opens will not be captured.
One indicator that this has happened is there is a low number of opens, but a high number of clicks.
However even if the open is not captured because of this, events such as clicks and bounces will still be tracked.
{}Tracking Results{}
My tracking can be organized into folders.
{}Speaker 1:{}
To keep organized, My Tracking allows you to create folders for your email sends.
In some instances your folders will auto-generate and send auto-filters for particular types like Test Send Emails, Triggered Sends and A/B Testing.
{}Customized Display{}
{}IN APPLICATION{}
<size val="2000">{}Speaker 1:{}

{}Toolbar Options{}
Move:
Move the email into another folder.
Delete:
Remove the email tracking from the application.
Cancel Send: stop a send in that is in progress.
Compare Email Sends:
Compares tracking data of one email to another email (more than one email must be selected).
Filter Options:
Change the number of {}emails{} or {}time since send{} to display.
Click the hyperlinked email name to access tracking data for that email.
{}IN APPLICATION{}

Aside from customizing your view, you also have additional options availability to you in the tool bar including:
Move – You’re able to move items from one folder into another.
Delete – you can remove email tracking data from the application
Cancel Send - stop a send that is currently underway.
Note that if you cancel a send it will not recall messages which have already been delivered.
Compare Email Sends – lets you compare tracking data of two or more email sends.
This a great tool to quickly review stats between two emails.
Filter Options - allows you to change the number or timeframe of emails displayed.
Finally, to access the tracking data for the job, click the hyperlinked name….

This tracking data is presented  in a graphical format.

Summary includes basic information about your send including the:

JOB ID (which is the unique identifier), the name and subject line, the date the email was sent and total sent (which may contrast the total delivered due to bounces.)

<fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx1&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;"> </fill-sd></size><size val="1400"><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx2&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">Remember open means images were rendered.

{}Animation 6:{}

We encourage you to include the Forward to a Friend feature in your marketing sends – this provides your subscribers a mechanism to share your email with friends they think will be interested, as well as a mechanism to protect their personal information and subscriptions in the subscription center.
{}Tracking Workspace – Click Activity{}
The Activity tab provides two views:
Email Overlay View
List View
{}IN APPLICATION{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
The second tab is the Activity tab that allows you to view the click activity your email received.
There are two views available in this area; The first one is the Email Overlay View, it displays a preview of the email with percentages next to any hyperlink in the email.
{}Animation 2:{}
The percentage represents the number of clicks compared to the number of people that opened the email.
{}Animation 3:{}
In this view, clicking the hyperlinked percentage will open a dialogue box displaying the actual click through rate, the percentage of total clicks (actual total clicks) and the percentage of unique clicks (with the actual number of unique clicks displayed).
The Email Overlay View is why you want to differentiate links in your emails when they link to the same url – because the clicks are tracked by the tracking alias.
On this tab we can view the percentage of clicks, identify our most popular links and ensure they are moved up in the email (especially those links below the fold).
This is also the tab you want to export when you want to demonstrate the success of your campaign in driving traffic.
{}Animation 4:{}
When you select export, and export it in PDF, the file will then generate what you are seeing on the screen.
{}Animation 5:{}
The List View is going to display a list of links and clicks.
By default it will be displayed in order of the hyperlink which was clicked most to the one that was clicked least.
In this view, clicking the actual hyperlink will take you to that webpage, such as your website or a registration form.
If you click the hyperlinked number of clicks you are taken to a list of subscribers who actually clicked that link.
<size val="1400"><fill-sd val="&lt;a:solidFill&gt;&lt;a:schemeClr val=&quot;tx2&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:solidFill&gt;">{}Animation 6:{}

This feature provides you a fantastic resource to consolidate your reporting by capturing conversions within the email application so you’ll be able to view the email, clicks and conversions all within one resource.

{}Tracking Workspace – Survey{}
{}IN APPLICATION<br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr sz=&quot;2400&quot; b=&quot;0&quot; i=&quot;1&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />{}{}Speaker 1:{}

On the right side of the screen, you’ll find the survey responses.

Number of completions and response rate are great to know, but how do you view how our subscribers responded?

{}Tracking Workspace – Job Links{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
The last tab you will see in the Tracking Workspace is the Job Links tab.
Sometimes you don’t catch a mistake, like a broken link in an email, until after you have hit send.
With our latest release, you can now edit a link in an email that has already been sent without having to reach out to Global Support.
It is important to note that only users with the Account Administer or Content Creator roles can edit links after an email is sent and you must be allowing the Marketing Cloud to track your click data.
{}Animation 1:{}
To edit the link, click on the URL ID associated with the link you are needing to edit.
When you are editing a link via the Job Links tab in Tracking, it is important to note that you are only changing the link for that specific Job ID and not the source email.
To ensure an edit is applied to the source email, you will need to navigate back to the content tab and make the edit there as well.

{}Using Tracking Data{}
{}Speaker 1:{}
Now that you have all this tracking data, you are probably wondering what you can do with it!
There are several ways to use data in the tracking area and we will review common uses next.
For example, you can create a list, export subscriber data from tracking to an excel file, export the bounce reason and bounce description, compare the tracking results, or create PDF and Excel files of the tracking tabs.
Let’s start with how to create a list from tracking data…
{}Create a List from Tracking Data{}
{}IN APPLICATION<br val="&lt;a:br&gt;&lt;a:rPr b=&quot;0&quot; i=&quot;1&quot; baseline=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a:br&gt;" />{}{}Speaker1:{}
Whenever you drilldown in the tracking data to view subscribers who did (or did not) take a particular action, you have the opportunity to add those subscribers to a list.
You can add subscribers to a preexisting list, or create a new one within the workflow.
Some great ways to apply this feature are to create a list of subscribers who clicked on a specific link to send a retargeted email, thank survey respondents for their participation in a survey, or to identify unengaged subscribers.
Let’s see how easy it is to create a list from tracking,
{}Animation 1:{}
Click the Copy All button in the toolbar,
{}Animation 2:{}
Then either select a list to add subscribers to, or create a list by selecting the New List radio button and entering the required List Name, though the description and marking public are optional.
{}Animation 3:{}
Then click Copy in the toolbar.
{}Exporting Subscriber Tracking Data{}
Subscriber data can also be exported to an Excel file (csv, tab delimited, or XML format).
{}Speaker1:{}
IN APPLICATION

{}Animation 1:{}

{}Animation 2:{}

This can be exported to your FTP, or attached in an email (if you don’t have FTP configured).
{}Animation 3:{}

{}Export Bounce Reason and Bounce Description{}

{}Animation 4:{}

Configure the remaining settings just like we did to export subscribers for delivery…
{}Animation 5:{}…and click Export in the toolbar when you’re done.
You can then use this data to either update your CRM system, determine which subscribers need contacted through another channel, or determine systemic issues your sends could be experiencing.

*The reports tool is a data analytics tool available in the marketing cloud.
The reports tool allows you to easily measure multiple campaigns and their success.*
*It also provides a larger perspective on multichannel strategies delivering additional insights into what’s happening with all your digital communications.*
*The reports tool is simple to use.
And it delivers real time detailed results of your data from your marketing campaigns.
It also provides a wide variety of report types that best feature needs.*
*There are three types of reports that are available in the reports tool:
Standard, Custom and Discover.
You’ll learn more about each of these types of report later in this module.*
*To learn how to access the reports tool click ‘next’.*
*Click next to continue.*
*The Reports Tool can be found in the exacttarget marketing cloud.
To access the Reports tool you will click on Reports in the Marketing cloud app switcher.*
*You will then be taken to overview page.
On the overview page there will be three ways to access every report.*
*You can click on catalog in the tool bar or if you defined the specific report as a shortcut, you can click on that specific report.*
*You can also access a category of reports via the report catalog area.
The report catalog area will list all the reports categories available in you account.*
*In this account we have custom reports, discover reports, email reports as well as mobile connect and social pages reports. *
*The workspace below will display all of the report perimeter definitions that you have saved when creating reports in the past.*
*The very left hand side will allow you to filter those reports for quick and easy access.*
*The reports tool offers 3 types of reports:
Standard, Custom and Discover reports.*
*Each comes with various features and functionality that provides tailored options to review the data needed for your marketing campaigns.
Standard reports are available on all accounts.*
*The Custom and Discover reports are available for an additional cost.
Now let’s take a deeper dive into the different report types.*
*Click on the report type to review more information about each one.
Then, click ‘next’ to continue.*
*Standard reports allow you to access new and legacy reports previously run in each channel application.*
*All standard reports for the email application, mobile connect and social pages are available in the reports tool, making it easy to run any report from a single tool.*
*The report catalogue area on the overview page will list the channel applications available on your account and the number of reports associated with the channel.*
*In this example there are 41 standard email reports, 5 mobile connect reports, and 3 standard social pages reports.*
*Welcome to the ‘Reports Tool Overview’ module.*
*A standard report is a document that contains statistics or data usually over a period of time.
The layout and the standard information that will be included in the report are defined and cannot be altered.*
*When you run a standard report, you will specify certain report parameters.
Report parameters can vary depending on the report being run.*
*For example when running the campaign ‘Email Tracking’ report, you will need to specify the date range, a specific campaign, exclusions, time zone and the date format.*
*While the account ‘Send Summary’ has you specify, the date range, exclusions, time zone and date format.*
*Custom reports are created upon request.*
*These reports are viewable in the catalogue and are created when our Standard or Discover reports do not provide the information based on your specific use case.*
*In most cases the Premium reporting solution Discover will provide the data necessary as well as the flexibility to create a report based on your specific needs.*
*Discover is a premium reporting tool that gives immediate views into your marketing metrics.*
*Discover lets you control the report presentation and content, delivering speed of thought insights into crosstab PivotTable style reports.*
*It also has a rich interactive visualization based on data that is refreshed daily.*

*What is a report?
A report provides you aggregate information about subscribers, sending, and other aspects of your email, mobile connect, mobile push or social pages applications.*
*There are three types of reports:
Standard, Custom and Discover.
Standard reports are available on all accounts.
Custom reports are being created specifically for your needs and Discover is our premium reporting tool.*

*In this lesson, you’ll learn five ways to deliver and schedule a report.*
*The report can be saved or you can use one of the delivery or scheduling options available in the reports tool.*
*The final report option is the schedule option.
The schedule option allows you to take a report definition that has been saved and establish a recurring schedule for the report to be run.*
*The report then can be emailed, placed on an FTP or saved as a snapshot.
It’s important to note that the scheduling option is only available for reports that have been created via the reports tool.*
*Any report that’s been created via the reports tool cannot be added as a step in a program or in automation via Automation Studio.*
*To learn more about the scheduling option, click the ‘schedule’ icon.*
*In this interactive simulation, you’ll learn how to schedule a report.*
*Once the report definition has been created, you can save it and establish a recurring schedule.
In order for the ‘schedule’ icon to become active, you must first save your report definition.*
*After saving your report definition, click on the ‘schedule’ icon.*
*After clicking on the ‘schedule’ icon, the schedule report results dialogue box will appear.
The report name will be-pre populated with the name you gave the report when the report was saved.*
*The first parameter you will define is the start date.
You will click on the calendar and select a date for the schedule to start.

*Once the start date has been selected, you will select a time for the report to run.
Click on the dropdown arrow to select a time.*
*From the dropdown select 7 AM as the start time.*
*If you need to select a different time zone for the report to run, click the dropdown, and then select the appropriate time zone.*
*Once you’ve established the date for the schedule to start, and a time to run the report, you’ll then select how often the report needs to be run.
Click on the dropdown.*
*You can choose to run a report once, hourly, daily, on the weekdays, weekly, monthly or yearly.
Depending on your selection, the repeat options will vary.
Select weekly.*
*When selecting the weekly option, you can run a report every week, every two weeks and so on.
We will run the report every week.*
*You will then select what day, or days of the week to run the report.
For example: you can select to run the report every Monday, Wednesday and Friday.*
*The default is Sunday.
In our example we will run the report every Monday morning.
You will begin by de-selecting Sunday.
Click on ‘Sunday’.*
*There are five options for delivering and scheduling a report.*
*To select Monday click on ‘Monday’.*
*After selecting when to run the report, you will then determine when the schedule will end.
You have two options: on date, and after.*
*The ‘after’ option will allow you to set the number of recurrences before the schedule will end.
The ‘on date’ option allows you to enter a date to stop the schedule.*
*We will select the default ‘on date’.
We will stop the program on January 1{}st{} 2015.
We will enter this for you.
Simply click in the textbox.*
*You can email the report, upload the report to the exact target and handstaff TP, download the report to your computer, save a snapshot of the report, or schedule the report to run on a recurring basis.*

*The process for creating a report starts with selecting the appropriate report to run.*
*Snapshot is another option available to view your report.
When saving a report as a snapshot, you are saving that version of the report to an online file folder located in the reports tool.*
*This option is very useful for online collaboration.
For example: a group of people needs to review the ‘complaints by domain’ report every Monday morning, and compare the data to pass through ports.*
*Instead of emailing the report to everyone each week, the report can be saved as a snapshot.
People are able to see the most current version of the report in addition to any other previous snapshots that have been saved.*
*You are able to access the snapshot feature after you’ve saved your report definition.*
*After selecting the report you will define the parameters for the report.*

Starting from the initial screen in Social Studio, click on the avatar on the upper right-hand corner.
Click Admin to access the admin screen.
To add a user, click Add New.
The username should not have any spaces; just use an underscore.
Fill in an email address.
Fill in the user information.
You have a few different options for language, as well as time zone.
A full user can create most types of resources.
Social Studio assigns this user role by default when you add a new user to the organization.
Social Studio restricts editing and deleting permissions to content owned by the full user.
Full users can generally create, view, and edit their own settings.
Full users cannot generally change user settings for other users.
Next, you need to assign this user a role.
The options are super user, full user, basic user or admin only user.
A super user can create, view, edit and disable or delete all system resources.
Super users can also perform all system tasks including editing users and workspaces and resetting passwords.
Super user is the highest level of access.
A basic user can view other users in the organization, and change their own personal information.
Basic users can also view and change any posts they created, and any posts that other users shared in the workspaces where they are a member.
For security purposes, basic users cannot change any organization settings.
Similar to a super user, the admin only user role can perform administrative tasks to protect content security and corporate image by preventing publishing, engaging, and analysis access.
They cannot create new workspaces, access the Engage console, the analysis dashboard, or the Social Studio mobile app.
The status is active for this new user.
Click the Add to Workspace button.
On the right, you will see all of the workspace options appear.
Choose NTO Training and click Add.
The workspace appears under the workspace section.

Intro to Topic Profiles
{}Introduction to Topic Profiles{}
{}After completing training you will be able to:{}
Create a topic profile in Social Studio.
Use topic profiles within engage and analyze in Social Studio.
Manage topic profiles within the admin tool.
{}Click Next {}to continue.
Upon completion of this course, you will expand your knowledge on where and how to use and integrate topic profiles, including using the Engage column and the Analyze dashboard.
Introduction to Topic Profiles
{}Introduction to Topic Profiles{}
{}What are Topic Profiles?{}
A Topic Profile is a social media search, created in Social Studio, comprised of keywords, sources, and filters.
Once a Topic Profile is created, the social media posts can be applied to Engage columns, allowing for workflow management and engagement from your own social media accounts.
In Analyze, multiple Social Listening Summary dashboards can be created using a different Topic Profile.
{}Click Next {}to continue.
Introduction
{}Features of Topic Profiles{}
With Topic Profiles you can:
Create searches with multiple keywords
Adjust keyword proximity
Categorize searches using keyword group
Filter topic profiles by language, media type, and region
Share topic profiles between workspaces
{}Click Next {}to continue.
{}Introduction to Topic Profiles{}
More information

{}Click {}the {}laptop{} to learn more.
Topic Profiles can be accessed under the Admin section in Social Studio.

11.6 Click
Click on the avatar in the upper right corner and choose Admin.
Click Add New under Topic Profiles.
Name the keyword group NTO Products.
Northern Trails TP
This brings up the Create Topic profile panel.
This topic profile will be about Northern Trail Outfitters, so name this topic profile
Under Type, choose Brand.
Keywords should pertain to the brand and how it is most commonly mentioned on social media.
The first keyword is NTO.
Click Done.
To add another keyword, click the plus button.
We'll add Northern Trails.
Keywords are not case sensitive, so capitalization does not matter.
Define conversations specifically about camping in the End Contains Keyword section.
Add keywords camping, tents and hiking.
You can also exclude conversations.
Say NTO is a local band, and you don't want to bring in conversations around NTO the band.
Exclude the keyword “music”.
You can also customize something called Keyword Proximity.
Click Northern Trails.
Now the words "Northern Trails" must appear right next to each other.
This is so that you don't have conversations brought in that have "Northern" in the first sentence and "Trails" in the third sentence.
Those conversations would not apply.
You can adjust this to have words in between.
For now, keep it with No Proximity.
With all the keywords filled out, click Create Keyword Group.
Filter options are Languages, Media Types, and Regions.
For Languages, deselect All Languages.
Select English and Spanish.
Click Save.
For Media Types{}Deselect Aggregator and Buy and Sell.
For Regions{}Deselect All
Choose Spain and The United States.
If you want to add another keyword group just click Add Keyword Group.
You could create a new keyword group to monitor a competitor's mentions.
Source groups enable tracking and managing of social listening sources that are important to your company.
To add a source group, go to the Source Group section and click Add.
Here you will find a list of previously created groups.
Search for the NTO Facebook and Twitter source groups, which were previously created.
Click the check box{}and click Save.
To remove a source group, search again.
You can also create a new source group from this panel view.
Click Save.
You might want to monitor just one source coming from a person whose opinion is very important to your company.
To do this, add a source group.
And find the previously created source group or create a new one.
To find out what the Sarah Smith Facebook profile is saying about your brand, copy her Facebook link
and click Add.
Name the source group
and click Save
to add this to the topic profile.
You can share this topic profile with a specific workspace.
You can also share with multiple workspaces.
To do this, go to the Sharing tab.
This topic profile is not shared with any workspace.
Click Edit Workspaces to see the list of workspaces within our tenant.
Share it with NTO Training
and click Apply.
This is to allow Full users, Basic users and users other than Super users to use the Topic Profile in the Workspace.
Now that you have created a topic profile, you will create an analyze dashboard called a social listening summary dashboard and apply the topic profile.
Click on Analyze at the top of the page.
To create a new dashboard, click Create New.
Choose Social Listening Summary.
This is the dashboard where you can apply a topic profile.
Since you shared this topic profile with the NTO Training workspace, which you are in now, you see it in this list.
To apply this topic profile, click the check mark next to it.
Click Create Dashboard.
This will create a social listening summary dashboard with the Northern Trails topic profile.
Here you can see common social metrics around Northern Trails.
On the left, you see a feed of mentions of Northern Trails.
You have post volume and posts over time.
You have keywords, what people are saying.
You also have volume by keyword group, top countries, top languages, sentiment, and sentiment over time.
All of these metrics focus just on camping conversations and the Northern Trail Outfitters brand because you applied the Northern Trails topic profile.
To create a topic profile column in Engage, start in the Engage tool and click Add Column.
This time you will add a Topic Profile.
Here you see the list of available topic profiles within the workspace NTO Training.
Click on the Northern Trails topic profile
and click Apply.
This will bring up a column that has applied our Topic Profile.
These are all the Northern Trail Outfitters mentions around camping, hiking and tents.
Managing topic profiles through searching and sorting is simple.
You have a long list of topic profiles within your workspace.
To pull up the Northern Trails topic profile you can search to find it.
You can also sort topic profiles.
Click on Name to sort in alphabetical order,
Click again to show reverse order.
You can also sort by Owner.{}EMV,{}or Status.
As a super user, I can see all the topic profiles available within this tenant in the Admin and Topic Profiles view.
You can see here there are five different topic profiles within this tenant.
If I log in to the account of a full user,{}I can only see three topic profiles.
That is because a full user can only see the topic profiles that are shared with them.
If I click into this Northern Trails topic profile,{}I can see all the information,{}but I'm not able to edit any of it.
Only the super user can do that.
If you are a full user you can edit any topic profiles that you have created yourself.
As a full user you can apply the topic profiles that have been shared with your workspace to a dashboard or to an Engage column.
